### 1. Organizing Instruction and Study to Improve Student Learning

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: learning-engineering, cognitive-science, k-12, math-strategies, formative-assessment
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/1

Seven recommendations for using learning and study time effectively in subjects requiring content mastery (science, social studies, mathematics): spacing content review, alternating worked examples with practice problems, combining visual and verbal instruction, linking abstract and concrete concepts, strategic use of quizzes, efficient study time allocation, and deep explanatory questioning.

---

### 2. Using Student Achievement Data to Support Instructional Decision Making

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: learning-engineering, formative-assessment, k-12, data-sharing, professional-development
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/12

Five recommendations for leveraging student data to monitor academic progress and evaluate teaching: establishing schoolwide data systems, fostering a data-informed culture, integrating data review into instructional improvement cycles, teaching students to interpret their own performance data for goal-setting, and implementing district-level evidence infrastructure.

---

### 3. Improving Mathematical Problem Solving in Grades 4 Through 8

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, math-word-problems, math-strategies, learning-engineering
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/16

Prepared by Mathematica. Five recommendations for teachers, math coaches, and curriculum developers targeting grades 4–8: preparing problems for whole-class instruction, supporting student self-monitoring and reflection, teaching visual representation, exposing students to multiple solution strategies, and helping students recognize mathematical concepts and notation.

---

### 4. Teaching Math to Young Children

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, early-childhood, prekindergarten, k-12, learning-engineering
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/18

Five recommendations for preschool, prekindergarten, and kindergarten educators: teaching number and operations using developmental progression (Moderate Evidence), teaching geometry and patterns developmentally (Minimal Evidence), using progress monitoring aligned to individual child knowledge (Minimal Evidence), teaching mathematical perspectives on everyday situations (Minimal Evidence), and dedicating daily math time integrated throughout instruction (Minimal Evidence). Each recommendation includes implementation steps and solutions for common obstacles.

---

### 5. Teaching Academic Content and Literacy to English Learners in Elementary and Middle School

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: english-learners, k-12, learning-engineering, professional-development
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/19

Four recommendations for elementary and middle school educators: intensive academic vocabulary instruction using varied activities, integration of oral and written English instruction into content areas, structured opportunities for written language development, and small-group interventions for struggling learners. Includes examples aligned to Common Core standards.

---

### 6. Teaching Strategies for Improving Algebra Knowledge in Middle and High School Students

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, math-strategies, learning-engineering
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/20

Three recommendations for middle and high school algebra educators: analyzing algebraic reasoning, utilizing structural representations, and selecting alternative problem-solving approaches. Each recommendation includes implementation steps and common roadblocks.

---

### 7. Using Technology to Support Postsecondary Student Learning

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: higher-ed, digital-learning-platforms, personalized-learning, learning-engineering
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/25

Five recommendations for higher education instructors, instructional designers, and administrators: use of communication tools, digital resources, self-regulated learning strategies, performance feedback, and simulation technologies for problem-solving. Targets postsecondary settings.

---

### 8. Assisting Students Struggling with Mathematics: Intervention in the Elementary Grades

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, math-strategies, learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/26

Six recommendations for grades K–6, all with strong evidence ratings: systematic instruction, mathematical language instruction, use of concrete representations, number line application, word problem instruction, and timed activities to build fluency. Covers both general student populations and children with disabilities.

---

### 9. Preparing Young Children for School

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: early-childhood, prekindergarten, k-12, learning-engineering
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/30

Seven recommendations distilling contemporary early childhood and preschool research to help prepare young children to benefit from educational opportunities in school settings.

---

### 10. CAST Universal Design for Learning Guidelines 3.0

Type: framework | Source: CAST
Tags: learning-engineering, k-12, inclusive-design, cognitive-science
URL: https://udlguidelines.cast.org

Organization: CAST. An educational framework "based on scientific insights into how humans learn" designed as "a tool that can be applied in any discipline or domain to ensure that all learners are able to access and participate in meaningful, challenging learning opportunities." Version 3.0 specifically addresses "critical barriers rooted in biases and systems of exclusion for learners with and without disabilities." Three design principles: Engagement, Representation, and Action & Expression. Overarching goal: learner agency that is "purposeful & reflective, resourceful & authentic, strategic & action-oriented." Downloadable PDF available in 20+ languages. Audience: educators, curriculum developers, learning and instructional designers, researchers, parents.

---

### 11. Recommendation on the Ethics of Artificial Intelligence

Type: framework | Source: UNESCO
Tags: ai-policy, ai-ethics, k-12, higher-ed
URL: https://www.unesco.org/en/articles/recommendation-ethics-artificial-intelligence?hub=195885

Adopted 2021, published 2022. UNESCO's inaugural global standard on AI ethics, addressed to all 194 UNESCO member states. Establishes that "the protection of human rights and dignity is the cornerstone" of the framework. Covers transparency, fairness, and human oversight of AI systems across Policy Action Areas addressing data governance, environmental concerns, gender equity, education, research, health, and social wellbeing.

---

### 12. UNESCO AI Competency Framework for Students

Type: framework | Source: UNESCO
Tags: ai-policy, k-12, higher-ed, ai-ethics, llm-application
URL: https://www.unesco.org/en/articles/what-you-need-know-about-unescos-new-ai-competency-frameworks-students-and-teachers

Four core competency areas for students (K-12 and higher education): "a human-centred mindset," "ethics of AI," "AI techniques and applications," and "AI system design." Direct PDF available in English, Arabic, French, Portuguese, Spanish, and Vietnamese at unesdoc.unesco.org (access from direct UNESDOC URL was blocked during audit; description sourced from UNESCO article page).

---

### 13. UNESCO AI Competency Framework for Teachers

Type: framework | Source: UNESCO
Tags: ai-policy, professional-development, k-12, higher-ed, ai-ethics, llm-application
URL: https://www.unesco.org/en/articles/what-you-need-know-about-unescos-new-ai-competency-frameworks-students-and-teachers

Five competency areas for teachers and educators: "a human-centred mindset," "ethics of AI," "AI foundations and applications," "AI pedagogy," and "AI for professional development." Direct PDF available in English, Arabic, French, Portuguese, Spanish, and Vietnamese at unesdoc.unesco.org (access from direct UNESDOC URL was blocked during audit; description sourced from UNESCO article page).

---

### 15. EMERALDS: Preparation for Success in Algebra

Type: report | Source: Carnegie Mellon University / Educational Testing Service
Tags: math-education, k-12, longitudinal, math-strategies, learning-engineering, cmu-learnlab, carnegie-learning
URL: https://achievethecore.org/page/3367/preparation-for-success-in-algebra-exploring-math-education-relationships-by-analyzing-large-data-sets-emeralds

Principal Investigator: David C. Geary (University of Missouri). Institutions: Human-Computer Interaction Institute at Carnegie Mellon University and Educational Testing Service. "One of the largest longitudinal assessments of what mathematics prepares students for success in Algebra" — uses anonymized large-scale data to identify mathematical competencies in earlier grades that form critical foundations for algebraic success, with particular focus on historically underserved student populations. Report hosted at Achieve the Core; full report linked from that page.

---

### 16. Lenses on Literature — Evidence for ESSA

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: k-12, computer-assisted-learning, carnegie-learning, learning-engineering, formative-assessment
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/lenses-on-literature/

Evidence review published at Evidence for ESSA (Johns Hopkins University). Carnegie Learning's Lenses on Literature (formerly Literacy Design Collaborative) earned a "Promising" (Tier 3) ESSA evidence rating. Instructional framework emphasizing daily, standards-driven reading, writing, and discourse organized around disciplinary literacy with complex texts. Primary study: 18,203 students across Kentucky and Pennsylvania (2012–2013). Effect size: +0.05 average; Kentucky: +0.06 (statistically significant); Pennsylvania: +0.03 (non-significant). Includes scaffolds for multilingual learners, embedded assessments using Stanford-aligned rubrics, and professional development with coaching and data analysis.

---

### 17. The State of Educational Data Mining in 2009: A Review and Future Visions

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, meta-analysis, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/8

Journal of Educational Data Mining, Vol. 1, No. 1. Inaugural-issue review paper for the EDM field: examines the history and methodological evolution of educational data mining, comparing early approaches with 2008–2009 research. Identifies three field-wide trends: increased emphasis on prediction methods, emergence of discovery-with-models techniques, and declining focus on relationship mining. Catalogues the most-cited EDM papers published 1995–2005 and analyzes their influence within and beyond the field. Open access under CC BY-NC-ND 4.0.

---

### 18. Breaking With the Past: Embracing Digital Transformation in Education

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: digital-learning-platforms, personalized-learning, learning-engineering, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/6559b261-d6d7-4184-9116-16eb93a9c212

Digital Promise report arguing for digital transformation of teaching and learning at scale across U.S. schools. Compares traditional one-size-fits-all instruction to learner-centered, personalized frameworks and examines how digital technologies can enable the transition—drawing on how other industries have used innovation to drive systemic change.

---

### 19. Computational Thinking for an Inclusive World

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, computer-assisted-learning, learning-engineering, digital-promise, inclusive-design
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/handle/20.500.12265/138

Digital Promise report calling on educators to integrate computational thinking across PreK–12 disciplinary learning with an explicit equity focus, addressing persistent gaps in access to computing education for marginalized students. Argues that CT skills are important for all students—not only future computer science students—and issues two calls to action for designing inclusive computing learning opportunities.

---

### 20. Shifting Mindsets: Designing Lessons for Learner Variability

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: personalized-learning, professional-development, learning-engineering, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/handle/20.500.12265/157

Digital Promise pilot study conducted with DonorsChoose examining whether teachers could use the Learner Variability Navigator (LVN)—a free, open-source web app curating whole-child research and evidence-based strategies—to customize instruction for diverse learners. Found that even brief use of the tool encouraged teachers to apply research-based strategies addressing learner variability across PreK–12 classrooms.

---

### 21. Assisting Students Struggling with Mathematics: Response to Intervention (RtI) for Elementary and Middle Schools

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, response-to-intervention, math-strategies, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/2

Eight recommendations for elementary and middle school math intervention using the Response to Intervention framework: screen all students and provide targeted support (Moderate), emphasize whole numbers K–5 and rational numbers grades 4–8 (Minimal), use explicit and systematic instruction (Strong), teach problem solving via common structural patterns (Strong), incorporate visual representations (Moderate), build fact fluency with approximately 10 minutes per session (Moderate), monitor student progress throughout intervention (Minimal), and include motivational strategies in secondary and tertiary intervention tiers (Minimal).

---

### 22. Assisting Students Struggling with Reading: Response to Intervention (RtI) and Multi-Tier Intervention in the Primary Grades

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, response-to-intervention, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/3

Five recommendations for primary-grade reading intervention using a multi-tier approach: screen all students for reading problems at the beginning and middle of the year (Moderate), provide differentiated reading instruction based on current assessments (Minimal), deliver intensive systematic instruction on up to three foundational reading skills in small groups for below-benchmark students (Strong), monitor tier 2 student progress monthly (Minimal), and deliver daily intensive instruction to tier 3 students showing minimal progress (Minimal).

---

### 23. Reducing Behavior Problems in the Elementary School Classroom

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: sel, k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/4

Five recommendations for elementary classroom behavior management: identify specific conditions triggering problem behavior (Moderate), modify the classroom environment to remove triggers (Strong), actively teach socially and behaviorally appropriate replacement skills (Strong), leverage relationships with colleagues, families, and behavioral experts (Moderate), and implement schoolwide prevention strategies requiring shared responsibility (Moderate).

---

### 24. Encouraging Girls in Math and Science

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/5

Five recommendations for broadening girls' participation in STEM: teach that academic abilities are expandable and improvable (Moderate), provide prescriptive informational feedback about student performance (Moderate), introduce female role models in math and science fields (Minimal), create learning environments that build curiosity and avoid gender stereotypes (Moderate), and integrate spatial skills training into instruction (Minimal).

---

### 25. Effective Literacy and English Language Instruction for English Learners in the Elementary Grades

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: english-learners, literacy, k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/6

Five recommendations for literacy instruction with elementary English learners: screen for reading problems and monitor progress in English (Strong), provide intensive small-group reading interventions for at-risk students (Strong), deliver extensive and varied vocabulary instruction throughout the school day (Strong), make formal academic English development a key instructional goal beginning in primary grades (Minimal), and schedule regular peer-assisted learning for structured academic collaboration approximately 90 minutes weekly (Strong).

---

### 26. Turning Around Chronically Low-Performing Schools

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/7

Four recommendations for school turnaround leaders: signal the need for dramatic change with leadership communicating urgency to staff and stakeholders; maintain a consistent focus on improving instruction by leveraging data to set goals and reassess learning continuously; make visible improvements early in the turnaround process to motivate staff and reduce resistance; and build a committed staff aligned with improvement objectives.

---

### 27. Improving Adolescent Literacy: Effective Classroom and Intervention Practices

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/8

Five recommendations for grades 5–12 literacy: provide explicit vocabulary instruction (Strong), deliver direct and explicit comprehension strategy instruction (Strong), facilitate extended discussion of text meaning and interpretation (Moderate), increase student motivation and engagement with reading (Moderate), and provide intensive individualized reading interventions by trained specialists for struggling readers (Strong).

---

### 28. Structuring Out-of-School Time to Improve Academic Achievement

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: k-12, personalized-learning, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/10

Five recommendations for administrators and educators designing out-of-school programs: align the OST program academically with the school day (Minimal), maximize student participation and attendance (Minimal), adapt instruction to individual and small group needs (Moderate), provide engaging learning experiences (Minimal), and assess program performance using results to continuously improve quality (Minimal).

---

### 29. Helping Students Navigate the Path to College: What High Schools Can Do

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: higher-ed, k-12, college-access, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/11

Five recommendations for high schools: provide college-preparatory coursework and ensure ninth graders understand college-readiness requirements; use ongoing assessments to monitor readiness and address skill gaps; foster college aspirations through supportive adult and peer networks; facilitate completion of essential college application steps (Moderate); and enhance financial literacy and support the financial aid application process (Moderate).

---

### 30. Improving Reading Comprehension in Kindergarten Through 3rd Grade

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, early-childhood, k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/14

Five recommendations for K–3 reading comprehension: train students to apply reading comprehension strategies (Strong), instruct students to leverage text structure for comprehension and retention (Moderate), facilitate substantive dialogue about textual meaning (Minimal), choose materials strategically to foster comprehension growth (Minimal), and establish an engaging and motivating context for reading instruction (Moderate).

---

### 31. Developing Effective Fractions Instruction for Kindergarten Through 8th Grade

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, math-strategies, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/15

Five recommendations for fractions instruction grades K–8: build on students' informal understanding of sharing and proportionality; establish that fractions are numbers that expand the number system beyond whole numbers; support understanding of the reasoning behind fraction computation procedures; develop conceptual understanding of ratio, rate, and proportion before introducing cross-multiplication; and improve teachers' own fraction knowledge through professional development. Emphasizes number lines as a central teaching tool across grade levels.

---

### 32. Teaching Elementary School Students to Be Effective Writers

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, writing-instruction, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/17

Four recommendations for grades 1–6 writing instruction: provide daily time for students to write (Minimal), teach students to use the writing process for a variety of purposes (Strong), teach fluency with handwriting, spelling, sentence construction, typing, and word processing (Moderate), and create an engaged community of writers (Minimal).

---

### 33. Foundational Skills to Support Reading for Understanding in Kindergarten Through 3rd Grade

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, early-childhood, k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/21

Four recommendations for K–3 foundational reading: teach academic language skills including inferential language and vocabulary (Minimal), develop phonological awareness and sound-letter links (Strong), teach decoding, word analysis, and written word recognition (Strong), and ensure each student reads connected text daily to build accuracy, fluency, and comprehension (Moderate).

---

### 34. Teaching Secondary Students to Write Effectively

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, writing-instruction, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/22

Three recommendations for grades 6–12 writing instruction across all subject areas: explicitly teach appropriate writing strategies using a Model-Practice-Reflect instructional cycle (Strong), integrate writing and reading to emphasize key writing features (Moderate), and use assessments of student writing to inform instruction and feedback (Minimal).

---

### 35. Strategies for Postsecondary Students in Developmental Education

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, personalized-learning, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/23

Six recommendations for college administrators, advisors, and faculty serving academically underprepared postsecondary students: use multiple measures to assess readiness and place students (Minimal), enhance advising through required or incentivized regular participation (Moderate), implement monetary performance incentives (Moderate), redesign developmental education through compression or mainstreaming (Minimal), teach self-regulated learning strategies (Minimal), and create comprehensive integrated support programs (Moderate).

---

### 36. Preventing Dropout in Secondary Schools

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: k-12, dropout-prevention, personalized-learning, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/24

Updated version of the 2008 dropout prevention guide, incorporating nine additional years of research. Four recommendations for grades 6–12: monitor all students and proactively intervene on early signs of attendance, behavior, or academic problems (Minimal); deliver tailored support to students who have fallen behind and face substantial barriers (Moderate); involve students through educational offerings bridging learning to college and career while building resilience (Strong); and for schools with many at-risk students, establish small personalized learning communities for better tracking and assistance (Moderate).

---

### 37. Designing and Delivering Career Pathways at Community Colleges

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: higher-ed, career-readiness, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/27

Five recommendations for community college administrators, faculty, and staff: structure pathways enabling students to advance education, secure employment, and progress professionally (Moderate); provide contextualized basic skills training accelerating pathway entry and completion (Moderate); offer flexible schedules and instructional models boosting credential completion (Minimal); coordinate comprehensive student services to enhance credit accumulation (Moderate); and develop strategic employer and community partnerships preparing students for labor market success (Moderate).

---

### 38. Effective Advising for Postsecondary Students

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, professional-development, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/28

Four recommendations for postsecondary advising: design comprehensive advising combining academic and non-academic supports (Moderate); build sustained, personalized advisor-student relationships throughout the college experience (Strong); employ mentoring and coaching to strengthen advising and support student achievement (Strong); and integrate positive incentives into advising structures to boost sustained student participation (Strong).

---

### 39. Providing Reading Interventions for Students in Grades 4–9

Type: framework | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, response-to-intervention, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/PracticeGuide/29

Four recommendations for grades 4–9 reading intervention: build students' decoding skills for complex multisyllabic words (Strong), provide purposeful fluency-building activities (Strong), implement interconnected comprehension practices covering vocabulary, question-and-answer activities, text-gist routines, and self-monitoring (Strong), and provide opportunities for students to practice with challenging stretch text (Moderate).

---

### 40. Knowledge is Power Program (KIPP) Charter Schools

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/688

WWC Intervention Report on KIPP, a nationwide network of free open-enrollment college-preparatory schools in under-resourced communities providing approximately 60% more instructional time than traditional public schools. Reviews 4 studies meeting standards out of 6 eligible. Found positive effects on mathematics and English language arts achievement, potentially positive effects on science and social studies achievement, and no discernible effects on student progression for grades 5–12.

---

### 41. Cognitive Tutor® Algebra I

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, learning-engineering, carnegie-learning, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/655

WWC Intervention Report on Cognitive Tutor® Algebra I, published by Carnegie Learning — a math curriculum combining textbooks with adaptive intelligent tutoring software. Reviews 6 studies meeting standards out of 18 eligible. Found positive effects on algebra achievement (grades 8–PS, Tier 1) and no discernible effects on general mathematics achievement in later grades (9–10).

---

### 42. Intelligent Tutoring for Structure Strategy (ITSS)

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/703

WWC Intervention Report on ITSS, a web-based supplemental program teaching students to identify and use text structure patterns (comparison, cause-effect, sequence, description, problem-solution) to improve literacy comprehension and recall in grades K–8. Reviews 2 studies meeting standards. Found positive effects on comprehension (grades 4–7, Tier 1).

---

### 43. Open Learning Initiative (OLI)

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: higher-ed, computer-assisted-learning, digital-learning-platforms, learning-engineering, cmu-learnlab, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/698

WWC Intervention Report on Carnegie Mellon University's Open Learning Initiative, offering innovative online courses designed to create high-quality learning experiences and advance educational research. Reviews 3 studies meeting standards out of 6 eligible. Found mixed effects on academic achievement and potentially positive effects on credit accumulation and persistence for postsecondary students.

---

### 44. DreamBox Learning

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, personalized-learning, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/627

WWC Intervention Report on DreamBox Learning, a supplemental online adaptive mathematics program for grades K–5 that individualizes instruction by creating unique paths through the curriculum matching each student's level of comprehension and learning style. Reviews 1 study meeting standards. Found potentially positive effects on general mathematics achievement (K–1, Tier 3), based on a predominantly Hispanic, English learner, urban sample.

---

### 45. READ 180®

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/665

WWC Intervention Report on READ 180®, a reading program combining online and direct instruction, student assessment, and teacher professional development for struggling readers 2+ years below grade level in grades 4–10. Reviews 9 studies meeting standards out of 39 eligible. Found positive effects on comprehension and general literacy achievement, potentially positive effects on reading fluency, and no discernible effects on alphabetics.

---

### 46. Achieve3000®

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, personalized-learning, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/691

WWC Intervention Report on Achieve3000®, a supplemental online literacy program providing differentiated nonfiction reading content for grades preK–12, targeting phonemic awareness, phonics, fluency, comprehension, vocabulary, and writing. Reviews 3 studies meeting standards out of 5 eligible. Found potentially positive effects on comprehension and general literacy achievement for adolescent readers (Tier 2).

---

### 47. Success for All®

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, response-to-intervention, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/672

WWC Intervention Report on Success for All® (SFA®), a whole-school reform model integrating curriculum, school culture, family, and community supports, emphasizing phonics for beginning readers and comprehension for all students in grades K–4. Reviews 9 studies meeting standards out of 49 eligible. Found positive effects on alphabetics, potentially positive effects on reading fluency, and mixed effects on comprehension and general reading achievement.

---

### 48. Self-Regulated Strategy Development (SRSD)

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: literacy, k-12, writing-instruction, response-to-intervention, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/680

WWC Intervention Report on SRSD, an intervention for grades 2–12 that improves academic skills through a six-step process teaching specific academic strategies and self-regulation, progressing from teacher-directed instruction to independent student application. Reviews 10 studies meeting standards out of 16 eligible. Based on single-case design studies, found potentially positive effects on writing achievement for students with specific learning disabilities (Tier 3).

---

### 49. Growth Mindset (Postsecondary)

Type: report | Source: What Works Clearinghouse
Tags: higher-ed, student-belonging, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/719

WWC Intervention Report reviewing growth mindset programs at the postsecondary level — interventions encouraging students to view intelligence as adaptable and academic challenges as surmountable. Reviews 6 studies meeting standards out of 10 eligible. Found potentially positive effects on academic achievement (Tier 2) and no discernible effects on college enrollment or progressing in college.

URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/695

WWC Intervention Report on ASAP, a three-year program removing barriers to associate degree completion by providing financial, academic, and personal supports while requiring full-time enrollment. Reviews 2 studies meeting standards out of 4 eligible. Found positive effects on access/enrollment, degree attainment, and credit accumulation/persistence (Tier 1 across all three outcome domains).

WWC Intervention Report on dual enrollment programs allowing high school students to take college courses and earn college credits, aimed at enhancing college access and degree completion for underrepresented students in grades 9–12. WWC Intervention Report on PALS, a peer-tutoring program for grades K–6 in which students take turns acting as tutor and tutee, coaching and correcting one another through literacy problems. WWC Intervention Report on Good Behavior Game, a classroom management strategy for grades K–11 that organizes students into teams and rewards appropriate conduct to improve social skills and minimize disruptive behaviors. Tags: literacy, k-12, response-to-intervention, learning-engineering, wwc
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/wwc/InterventionReport/475

WWC Intervention Report on Sound Partners, a phonics-based tutoring program providing supplemental reading instruction to grades K–3 students with below-average reading skills. Reviews 7 studies meeting standards out of 11 eligible. Found positive effects on alphabetics and reading fluency (Tier 3), potentially positive effects on comprehension, and no discernible effects on general reading achievement.

### 138. Effective Teacher Professional Development

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, learning-engineering, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/effective-teacher-professional-development

Learning Policy Institute research synthesis by Darling-Hammond, Hyler, and Gardner (2017) identifying seven features of effective teacher professional development across 35 rigorous studies. Finds effective PD is content-focused, incorporates active learning, supports collaboration, models effective practice, provides coaching and expert support, offers feedback and reflection, and is sustained over time. Concludes that PD meeting these criteria demonstrably improves teacher practice and student learning outcomes.

---

### 139. Design Principles for Teacher Preparation: Enacting the Science of Learning and Development

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, learning-engineering, lpi, higher-ed
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/sold-design-principles-teacher-preparation-report

Learning Policy Institute report by Darling-Hammond, Hyler, Wojcikiewicz, and Rushing (2025) presenting five evidence-based design principles for teacher preparation programs grounded in the science of learning and development. Principles address: curriculum grounded in developmental understanding of learners; equitable educator mindsets and skills; rich experiential learning with feedback cycles; pedagogical alignment between teacher educators and candidates; and supportive developmental relationships within programs and PreK–12 school partnerships. Draws on neuroscience, developmental psychology, and exemplary program practices.

---

### 140. Community Schools Impact on Student Outcomes: Evidence From California

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, lpi, attendance, sel
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/ca-community-schools-impact-student-outcomes-report

Learning Policy Institute study by Swain, Leung-Gagné, Maier, and Rubinstein (2025) evaluating California's Community Schools Partnership Program (CCSPP), a $4.1 billion state initiative. Analyzes 458 schools using matched difference-in-differences methodology across 2018–19 through 2023–24. Finds 30% greater reduction in chronic absenteeism, ~15% decline in suspensions, and academic gains of 0.06 SD in math and 0.05 SD in ELA (~43 and ~36 additional learning days). Benefits were disproportionately large for Black students, English learners, and socioeconomically disadvantaged students.

---

### 141. The State of the Teacher Workforce

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, k-12, learning-engineering, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/state-of-teacher-workforce-interactive-0

Learning Policy Institute interactive report (updated July 2024) providing state-by-state analysis of teacher workforce conditions across all 50 U.S. states. Assigns each state a teaching attractiveness rating (1–5) measuring compensation, working conditions, and retention factors, and a teacher equity rating (1–5) assessing equitable distribution of qualified educators across demographic groups. Draws from national datasets for 2017–18 through 2022–23 academic years.

---

### 142. How People Learn: Brain, Mind, Experience, and School (Expanded Edition)

Type: report | Source: National Academies of Sciences, Engineering, and Medicine
Tags: learning-engineering, nap, k-12
URL: https://www.nationalacademies.org/read/9853/chapter/

National Research Council expanded edition report (2000) edited by Bransford, Brown, and Cocking synthesizing research on learning science across cognitive, developmental, and neuroscientific perspectives. Bridges theoretical findings with classroom practice by examining how expertise develops, how knowledge transfers, and how children acquire understanding. Provides evidence-based guidance for designing effective learning environments across history, mathematics, and science disciplines. Free online reading via National Academies Press.

---

### 143. How People Learn II: Learners, Contexts, and Cultures

Type: report | Source: National Academies of Sciences, Engineering, and Medicine
Tags: learning-engineering, nap, k-12, higher-ed
URL: https://www.nationalacademies.org/publications/24783

National Academies consensus report (2018) chaired by Cora B. Marrett updating the influential 2000 How People Learn volume. Synthesizes findings from cognitive neuroscience, educational research, and learning technologies with emphasis on sociocultural and environmental factors shaping learning across the lifespan. Addresses learning from infancy through adulthood in both formal and informal settings. Free online reading via National Academies Press.

---

### 144. CASEL SEL Framework

Type: framework | Source: Collaborative for Academic, Social, and Emotional Learning (CASEL)
Tags: sel, learning-engineering, casel, k-12, inclusive-design
URL: https://casel.org/fundamentals-of-sel/what-is-the-casel-framework/

CASEL framework (updated 2020) defining the five core social-emotional competencies — self-awareness, self-management, social awareness, relationship skills, and responsible decision-making — and their implementation across four settings: classrooms, schools, families and caregivers, and communities. The 2020 update strengthened the framework's equity orientation, emphasizing SEL's potential in promoting educational equity and excellence and its adaptability to local cultural contexts.

---

### 145. Engaging First: Supporting Young Learners Through Family Engagement

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: early-childhood, k-12, learning-engineering, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/resource/young-learners-family-engagement

EdTrust research brief by Ivy Morgan (2024) examining family-school partnerships for early elementary learners based on nationally representative surveys of 600 parents/caregivers and 300 teachers of first and second graders during 2022–23. Finds broadly positive communication overall but significant gaps: only ~two-thirds of parents had access to parent-teacher conferences; low-income and multilingual families faced greater barriers including unwelcoming school staff. Part of EdTrust's broader SEAD research program.

---

### 146. Making Assessment Reports More Meaningful for Students & Families

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: formative-assessment, k-12, learning-engineering, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/resource/assessment-reports-family-engagement

EdTrust report by Munyan-Penney and Levitan (2024) providing guidance for schools on improving communication of federally required annual assessment results to students and families. Advocates for integrating score reports into existing family communications, identifies best practices for accessible report design, and offers policy recommendations for advocates and state leaders to improve assessment reporting at scale.

---

### 147. How Student, Family, and Community Engagement Impacts Students' SEAD

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: sel, k-12, learning-engineering, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/resource/student-family-community-engagement-sead

EdTrust report by Duchesneau and Wriston (2024) examining how school, family, and community engagement supports students' social, emotional, and academic development (SEAD). Identifies obstacles to meaningful engagement and provides policy recommendations for federal, state, and local decision-makers. Part of EdTrust's broader research on whole-child development and the role of family-school partnerships in student wellbeing and academic outcomes.

---

### 148. Funding Gaps 2018

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/resource/funding-gaps-2018/

EdTrust report by Morgan and Amerikaner (2018) documenting school funding disparities across U.S. states and districts. Finds districts serving predominantly students of color receive ~$1,800 (13%) less per student in state and local funding than majority-white districts; high-poverty districts receive ~$1,000 (7%) less than low-poverty districts. Gap widens to $2,000 per student (16%) when adjusted for additional costs of supporting low-income students. Documents state-by-state variation and highlights states achieving more equitable funding.

---

### 149. Teacher Turnover in the United States: Who Moves, Who Leaves, and Why

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, k-12, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/teacher-turnover-united-states-report

This comprehensive analysis examines why approximately 1 in 7 public school teachers annually leave their schools or exit the profession, using national data from 2020–22. The report finds that turnover rates have increased roughly 27% since the early 1990s, with disparities concentrated in schools serving predominantly low-income students and students of color. Three primary factors significantly influence retention: teacher salaries, effective school leadership, and overall job satisfaction tied to classroom autonomy and collegial support.

---

### 150. Supporting and Sustaining a Diverse Teacher Workforce

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, k-12, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/diverse-teacher-workforce-report

This report examines why teachers of color leave the profession at higher rates than their white counterparts and identifies systemic barriers to their retention. Using national survey data from 2017–2021, researchers found that teachers of color face less access to comprehensive preparation, competitive salaries, mentoring support, and positive working environments. The study emphasizes that while recruiting more educators of color matters, retention through improved conditions and support systems is equally critical to building a stable, diverse teaching force.

---

### 151. Untangling the Evidence on Preschool Effectiveness: Insights for Policymakers

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: early-childhood, prekindergarten, meta-analysis, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/untangling-evidence-preschool-effectiveness-report

This report synthesizes rigorous evaluations of 21 public preschool programs to clarify conflicting findings about whether quality early childhood education produces meaningful gains for students. The research demonstrates that high-quality preschool leaves children better prepared for school, especially in academic skill development, with benefits extending into adulthood through higher graduation rates and earnings. The report identifies six essential quality elements—including small class sizes, well-trained teachers, developmentally appropriate curricula, and family engagement—and notes that effective programs generate up to $17 in social returns for every dollar invested.

---

### 152. Community Schools as an Effective School Improvement Strategy: A Review of the Evidence

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, student-belonging, sel, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/community-schools-effective-school-improvement-report

This comprehensive report synthesizes findings from 143 rigorous research studies examining how community schools impact student and school outcomes, identifying four core pillars of effective implementation: integrated student supports, expanded learning time, family and community engagement, and collaborative leadership. The study demonstrates that community schools help disadvantaged students overcome barriers to learning by integrating academic instruction with health services, youth development, and community partnerships. The evidence base meets federal requirements under the Every Student Succeeds Act, providing policymakers with research-backed guidance for implementing community schools as an equitable school improvement strategy.

---

### 153. Coaching at Scale: A Strategy for Strengthening the Early Learning Workforce

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: early-childhood, coaching, professional-development, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/coaching-at-scale-report

This report examines five early childhood coaching systems across Alabama, Washington, and California to understand how comprehensive coaching can be implemented at scale to improve educator practice and program quality. The research identifies that effective coaching relies on strong partnerships, individualized feedback, focused observations, and well-qualified coaches with expertise in child development and adult learning. The report provides policymakers with eight actionable recommendations, including dedicated funding for coaching, establishing coach qualification standards, and developing regional professional development networks to sustain systemic improvements across the early learning workforce.

### 154. Reducing Chronic Absenteeism: Lessons from Community Schools

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, attendance, student-belonging, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/chronic-absenteeism-community-schools-report

This report examines how four California community schools successfully reduced chronic absenteeism following the pandemic, when national rates had nearly doubled to 28% by 2022. Key strategies included strengthening family engagement through outreach and home visits, building student connections through mentorship, systematically tracking attendance data, implementing tiered support systems, and leveraging community partnerships to address underlying barriers like housing and mental health needs. The findings emphasize that proactive and preventive approaches combined with trusting relationships prove more effective than punitive measures in addressing attendance challenges.

### 155. Strengthening the Educator Pipeline Through Service Scholarships: California's Golden State Teacher Grant Program

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, k-12, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/ca-golden-state-teacher-grant-program-report

This report evaluates California's Golden State Teacher Grant Program, which has distributed over $570 million since 2020–21 to help aspiring teachers afford preparation costs in exchange for committing to teach in high-need schools for two years, supporting more than 28,000 candidates and likely contributing to a 23% increase in California-prepared teachers earning credentials. Nearly 75% of survey respondents cited the grant as influential in their decision to pursue teaching, with particularly strong impact among candidates of color and career changers. The report recommends stable long-term funding benchmarked to cover significant portions of preparation costs, improved implementation support, and better data collection systems to track long-term outcomes.

### 156. High-Quality Early Childhood Assessment: Learning From States' Use of Kindergarten Entry Assessments

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: early-childhood, formative-assessment, prekindergarten, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/high-quality-kindergarten-entry-assessments-report

This report examines kindergarten entry assessments (KEAs) across states, noting that as of 2021, 38 states had adopted KEAs—a fivefold increase over a decade—though concerns arose about inappropriate practices like overly scripted assessments or narrow skill-focused measures that exclude essential developmental domains. The report emphasizes that high-quality KEA content aligns with developmentally appropriate kindergarten standards and measures multiple domains including social-emotional, cognitive, language, and physical development in culturally relevant ways. It recommends states select authentic assessments, build systems supporting teacher instruction and family engagement, and use data to strengthen learning systems rather than evaluate individual providers.

### 157. The Building Blocks of High-Quality Early Childhood Education Programs

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: early-childhood, prekindergarten, professional-development, english-learners, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/building-blocks-high-quality-early-childhood-education-programs

This policy brief identifies nine essential components that characterize effective pre-K programs, grounded in research demonstrating that high-quality early education generates approximately $7 in returns for every dollar invested. The report emphasizes that quality matters tremendously—particularly for low-income children and English learners—and establishes benchmarks including well-qualified teachers with bachelor's degrees in early childhood education, ongoing coaching and mentoring, support for diverse learners, meaningful family partnerships, small class sizes, and robust quality rating systems. These interconnected elements work together to foster the meaningful teacher-child interactions that research shows are fundamental to producing measurable gains in academic achievement and social-emotional development.

### 158. Community Schools Impact on Student Outcomes: Evidence From California

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, attendance, student-belonging, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/ca-community-schools-impact-student-outcomes-report

This report evaluates California's $4.1 billion Community Schools Partnership Program, the nation's largest state-level community schools initiative launched in 2021, using a matched difference-in-differences methodology comparing 458 CCSPP schools to similar non-recipient schools from 2018–19 to 2023–24. Researchers found that community school approaches led to a meaningful reduction in chronic absence averaging 30% greater than comparison schools, along with notable improvements in suspension rates and test scores. The most substantial gains benefited historically underserved students including Black students, English learners, and economically disadvantaged youth.

---

### 159. Teacher Residencies in Texas: Supporting Successful Implementation

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, k-12, coaching, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/texas-teacher-residencies-implementation-report

This report examines Texas's High-Quality, Sustainable Residencies Program, which funded over 85 teacher residency programs from 2021–2024 using COVID-19 relief money and provided stipends for more than 2,000 residents. The research identifies essential program features—including full-year classroom placements, $20,000 resident stipends, mentor teachers, and co-teaching models—as critical to successful implementation, while highlighting how strategic staffing models help districts sustain paid residencies beyond grant funding. The report concludes with six policy recommendations including requirements for research-based residency features, support for mentor teacher pipelines, and targeted funding for rural and high-poverty districts facing acute teacher shortages.

### 160. Diversifying the Teaching Profession: How to Recruit and Retain Teachers of Color

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, k-12, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/diversifying-teaching-profession-report

This report examines barriers that impede teachers of color from entering and remaining in the profession, while documenting how such teachers significantly benefit student outcomes. The research reveals that while recruitment has increased, attrition rates remain high, creating persistent supply-demand gaps particularly among Black, Native American, and Latinx educators. The study identifies three primary intervention areas: high-retention pathways into teaching through scholarships and residencies; hiring strategies that include diverse committees and early recruitment; and improving school conditions through better leadership preparation.

### 161. Design Principles for Teacher Preparation: Enacting the Science of Learning and Development

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: professional-development, k-12, sel, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/sold-design-principles-teacher-preparation-report

This report presents five design principles for teacher preparation programs that incorporate findings from neuroscience, developmental psychology, and learning sciences to help future educators support whole child development. The framework emphasizes that teacher candidates must themselves experience the very kinds of teaching strategies they are expected to develop for their pupils, ensuring teachers can authentically model approaches like inquiry-based learning and restorative practices. The principles address curriculum grounded in learning science, equitable educator mindsets, experiential learning opportunities, pedagogical alignment between university coursework and school placements, and the creation of supportive professional learning communities.

### 162. State Preschool in a Mixed Delivery System: Lessons From Five States

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: early-childhood, prekindergarten, professional-development, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/state-preschool-mixed-delivery-system-report

This report examines how five states—Alabama, Michigan, New Jersey, New York, and West Virginia—operate public preschool programs across diverse provider settings including school districts and community-based organizations. The study identifies key policy decisions regarding governance, quality standards, teacher compensation, and enrollment coordination that enable states to maintain consistent educational quality while serving children through multiple delivery channels. The authors recommend that states establish uniform quality benchmarks across all settings, remove barriers to non-LEA participation, provide sustained professional development, ensure competitive teacher compensation, implement coordinated enrollment systems, and collect demographic data to identify access disparities.

### 163. Developing Assessment Systems That Support Teaching and Learning: Recommendations for Federal Support

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: formative-assessment, k-12, ai-policy, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/developing-assessment-systems-federal-support-report

This report examines how the federal government can support states in transforming their assessment systems beyond traditional end-of-year multiple-choice tests, noting that more than 20 states are involved in efforts to transform one or more aspects of their assessment systems but face substantial barriers to federal approval. The authors identify three key recommendations for federal executive action: updating the Department of Education's peer review process to align with ESSA's encouragement of innovative assessments, strengthening the Innovative Assessment Demonstration Authority program to reduce burdensome requirements, and expanding funding pathways to incentivize state-level innovation in assessment design.

### 164. School Funding Effectiveness: Evidence From California's Local Control Funding Formula

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/school-funding-effectiveness-ca-lcff-report

This comprehensive study examines how California's 2013 Local Control Funding Formula—which directed $18 billion in increased state support to high-need districts over eight years—affected student outcomes across the state's 1,000 districts and 10,000 schools. Tracking 6.2 million K-12 students from 1995–96 through 2018–19, the research finds that a $1,000 per-pupil spending increase yielded full grade-level improvements in math and reading after three years, boosted high school graduation rates by 8.2 percentage points, and decreased suspensions and expulsions particularly for Black students. Instructional spending—class size reduction, teacher salary increases, and reduced turnover—accounted for roughly 84% of the variation in funding effectiveness.

---

### 165. Lost Opportunities: How Disparate School Discipline Continues to Drive Differences in the Opportunity to Learn

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, school-discipline, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/crdc-school-discipline-report

This report examines how out-of-school suspensions and other exclusionary discipline practices create substantial learning loss, with particularly severe impacts on students of color, secondary students, and those with disabilities. During the 2015–16 school year alone, the nation lost approximately 11.4 million instructional days due to suspensions—the equivalent of 62,596 years of lost learning. The research documents widespread racial disparities in discipline outcomes and significant failures by districts to report school-policing data as required by federal law.

---

### 166. Long-Term English Learners in California

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, english-learners, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/ca-long-term-english-learners-report

This report examines approximately 330,000 California students classified as English learners for 7 or more years, analyzing their demographics, school contexts, and academic outcomes compared to peers. The research reveals that long-term English learners are disproportionately boys (56%), economically disadvantaged (89%), and have higher special education needs (28%), while attending schools with fewer resources and lower graduation rates. Key recommendations include ensuring adequate schooling resources and whole-child supports, addressing teacher shortages in high-poverty schools, better identifying early learning needs for students with disabilities, and conducting further research on graduation barriers for this vulnerable population.

---

### 167. Investing for Student Success: Lessons From State School Finance Reforms

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, longitudinal, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/investing-student-success-school-finance-reforms-report

This report examines how U.S. public schools are inequitably funded through reliance on local property taxes and analyzes reform efforts in Connecticut, Massachusetts, New Jersey, and North Carolina that successfully improved educational resources and outcomes. The research demonstrates that when more money is spent on education, especially for students from low-income families, achievement and graduation rates improve alongside life outcomes like employment and wages. The report recommends federal and state actions—including equalizing funding allocations, ensuring qualified teachers reach high-poverty schools, and investing in quality preschool—as essential steps toward creating equitable learning opportunities for all students.

---

### 168. Advancing Integration and Equity Through Magnet Schools

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, school-discipline, student-belonging, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/advancing-integration-equity-magnet-schools-report

This report examines how magnet schools—public schools offering specialized programs to attract diverse student populations—can combat the alarming resegregation occurring in U.S. schools. The authors identify key components for success, including "first door" strategies like intentional family outreach and inclusive enrollment, plus "second door" approaches such as culturally responsive curriculum and restorative discipline practices. The report provides policy recommendations at federal, state, district, and school levels to help create and sustain magnet schools that achieve both integration and positive academic outcomes for all students.

### 169. Instructionally Relevant Assessment Systems: What is the Role of Performance Assessments?

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: formative-assessment, k-12, professional-development, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/instructionally-relevant-assessment-systems-report

This report examines how performance assessments—tasks requiring human scoring like constructed responses and essays—can transform state assessment systems to prioritize positive instructional impact alongside accountability functions. The author argues that because teachers inevitably take cues from state-level assessments to shape their instruction, assessment designers should intentionally leverage this influence by incorporating authentic performance tasks that signal high-quality teaching practices. The report provides system leaders with five strategic recommendations for balancing performance assessments with other instruments, emphasizing that well-designed tasks can generate reliable comparable scores while simultaneously improving what students learn and how teachers teach.

### 170. The Promise of Performance Assessments: Innovations in High School Learning and Higher Education Admissions

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: formative-assessment, k-12, higher-ed, college-access, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/promise-performance-assessments-report

This report examines how schools and colleges are adopting performance-based assessments—such as portfolios, capstone projects, and senior defenses—to evaluate deeper learning skills needed for college and career success. The authors document that more than 900 colleges have made standardized tests optional and are increasingly interested in reviewing broader student work samples for admission decisions. A key finding is that these assessments show particular promise for better reflecting the achievements and potential of historically underserved students, potentially addressing longstanding disparities in standardized testing outcomes across racial and socioeconomic lines.

This report examines innovative pathways for recruiting and preparing early childhood educators with a focus on creating accessible routes for diverse candidates, identifying three successful California programs that demonstrate how to support educators from underrepresented backgrounds through affordable, hands-on preparation models. The analysis reveals significant barriers early educators face when pursuing higher education, notably that low wages often make higher education costs prohibitively expensive. The report recommends that states invest in faculty development, clinical experiences, clear transfer pathways between community and four-year colleges, robust financial assistance, and coherent credential standards to ensure all young children have qualified teachers reflecting their communities' diversity.

### 172. Community Schools in Lynwood Unified: Building Capacity for Districtwide Implementation

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, attendance, professional-development, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/ca-community-schools-lynwood-unified-report

This report examines how Lynwood Unified School District successfully scaled community schools across all 17 campuses by strategically developing community school coordinators as implementation leaders, leveraging $24 million in state funding to expand from a single pilot school to a districtwide initiative. The district achieved measurable improvements including a one-third reduction in chronic absence, enhanced academic performance, and a 15.5% decline in suspensions within two years. The research highlights five critical implementation strategies including data-driven needs assessments, structured professional learning communities, and coaching networks that positioned coordinators as essential change agents rather than peripheral support roles.

### 173. State Strategies for Investing in Community Schools

Type: report | Source: Learning Policy Institute
Tags: k-12, student-belonging, sel, lpi
URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/state-strategies-investing-in-community-schools-report

This report examines how states are funding and supporting community schools by identifying three primary approaches: ongoing funding through school financing formulas (Maryland, New York), competitive grant programs (California, Illinois, New Mexico, Vermont), and capacity-building supports like certification processes (Florida, Georgia). State investments range from $3.4 million to $4.1 billion, with most states prioritizing schools serving high-poverty populations. Key findings show states are increasingly investing in evidence-based strategies including integrated student supports, expanded learning time, family engagement, and collaborative leadership structures that align with trauma-informed practices.

URL: https://learningpolicyinstitute.org/product/road-high-quality-early-learning-lessons-states

This report examines how four states—Michigan, West Virginia, Washington, and North Carolina—have built high-quality early education systems, drawing on policy reviews, program observations, and interviews with 159 stakeholders. The analysis identifies five overarching strategies these states employ: establishing quality standards and improvement systems, investing in educator development, coordinating birth-through-grade-3 programs, combining multiple funding sources, and building broad-based coalitions. The report provides policymakers with actionable insights on defining and using state quality standards, linking funding to ratings, investing in teacher training and coaching, and fostering cross-agency coordination to create seamless educational experiences for young learners.

High-achieving Black and Latino students and students from low-income backgrounds who pass Algebra I in eighth grade still enroll in advanced high school math at lower rates than their peers. Developed jointly with Just Equations, this brief documents enrollment disparities and identifies differences in teacher and counselor practices as contributing factors to these access gaps.

Schools often narrowly focus on changing student behavior rather than building relationships and supportive learning environments, disproportionately affecting students of color and low-income students. The report provides recommendations for state and district leaders to expand access and improve equity in advanced coursework enrollment.

### 181. 'Segregation Forever?': The Continued Underrepresentation of Black Undergraduates at the Nation's 122 Most Selective Private Colleges and Universities

URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/segregation-forever-the-continued-underrepresentation-of-black-undergraduates-at-the-nations-122-most-selective-private-colleges-and-universities/

EdTrust examined Black student enrollment at 122 selective private colleges and universities in 2000 and 2020, finding that despite nearly 74% of these institutions increasing Black enrollment, 71% still received failing grades for Black student access in 2020. The research reveals that gains were minimal and that elite institutions remain largely inaccessible to Black first-time undergraduates relative to state population demographics.

In nearly every state the affordability gap at four-year institutions exceeds $3,000, with the national average around $6,500.

### 190. Parent PLUS Loans Are a Double-Edged Sword for Black Borrowers

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/parent-plus-loans-are-a-double-edged-sword-for-black-borrowers/

This brief examines how Black parents increasingly rely on Parent PLUS loans to fund their children's college education, despite these loans carrying higher interest rates and less favorable terms than federal student loans. The report reveals that structural racism, including racial wage and wealth gaps, forces Black families to borrow heavily, and that Black parent borrowers struggle significantly with repayment — often deferring payments and drawing from retirement accounts at higher rates than White borrowers, creating a multigenerational toll of debt.

Drawing on qualitative data from EdTrust's National Black Student Debt Study, this brief examines how federal income-driven repayment plans are ineffective at reducing debt for Black borrowers. The authors argue that even recent administrative improvements do not address underlying college affordability issues or help future students, and recommend broad debt cancellation plus creation of a new repayment plan with more favorable terms.
