### 192. For Student Parents, The Biggest Hurdles to a Higher Education Are Costs and Finding Child Care

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, dropout-prevention, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/for-student-parents-the-biggest-hurdles-to-a-higher-education-are-costs-and-finding-child-care/

This report examines the financial barriers facing student parents, finding that there is no state in which a student parent can work 10 hours per week at minimum wage and afford both tuition and child care at a public college. Student parents face out-of-pocket costs that are 2 to 5 times higher than peers without children, requiring an average of 52 hours of weekly work per week to cover expenses.

---

### 193. Building a Diverse & Strong Educator Workforce for Students

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: k-12, professional-development, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/building-a-diverse-strong-educator-workforce-for-students/

This resource highlights a significant disparity in educator demographics: students of color make up more than 50% of the K-12 public school student population while teachers of color represent less than 20% of educators. Students from underserved backgrounds are four times more likely to attend schools with larger percentages of uncertified and inexperienced teachers, contributing to disparities in discipline rates, graduation outcomes, and educational access.

---

### 194. Access Granted: School Funding Between Schools in Districts

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: k-12, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/access-granted-school-funding-between-schools-in-districts/

EdTrust analyzed newly available school-by-school spending data required by the Every Student Succeeds Act to examine funding equity within districts. The analysis reveals that in 97% of districts included, state and local spending was flat or regressive for all student groups examined, with very few students of color, low-income students, or English learners attending schools where funding is allocated to meet their additional needs.

---

### 195. Reassessing ESSA Implementation: An Equity Analysis of School Accountability Systems

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: k-12, longitudinal, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/reassessing-essa-implementation-an-equity-analysis/

EdTrust examined how states implement federal school accountability requirements under the Every Student Succeeds Act, finding that states have a mixed record of centering equity in school ratings. The analysis identifies significant gaps in how states identify low-performing schools and support improvement efforts, and reveals that while some states show promising practices, most have failed to connect school identification processes to robust support systems that would meaningfully improve outcomes for historically underserved students.

---

### 196. Jim Crow Debt: How Black Borrowers Experience Student Loans

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, qualitative-research, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/jim-crow-debt/

This report presents findings from the National Black Student Loan Debt Study, based on a survey of nearly 1,300 Black borrowers and interviews with 100 participants. Key findings reveal that Black borrowers view student loans as problematic rather than beneficial, experience income-driven repayment plans as lifetime debt sentences, and overwhelmingly support complete government debt forgiveness as a racial justice solution, with the research connecting these outcomes to systemic racism and labor market stratification.

---

### 197. Creating Positive College Campus Racial Climates for Students of Color

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: higher-ed, student-belonging, qualitative-research, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/college-campus-racial-climates-2/

EdTrust interviewed 32 Black, Latino, and Asian American students at predominantly White institutions to understand how campus racial climate affects their experiences. The research identified key challenges including underrepresentation of students and faculty of color, limited institutional support, unclear reporting procedures for discrimination incidents, and insufficient mental health resources tailored to students of color.

---

### 198. How Student Debt Harms Black Borrowers' Mental Health

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: higher-ed, student-belonging, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/how-student-debt-harms-black-borrowers-mental-health/

Drawing on the National Black Student Debt Study, this brief examines the intersection of student debt and mental health among Black borrowers, finding that 64% of survey participants reported that student debt negatively impacted their mental health. The report documents how Black borrowers face disproportionate challenges with student loans due to structural racism and fewer generational resources, establishing that the psychological toll of debt can be as severe as its financial consequences.

---

### 199. How Black Women Experience Student Debt

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/how-black-women-experience-student-debt/

This brief examines how Black women are disproportionately affected by the student debt crisis due to intersecting discrimination and systemic inequities. Using federal data and the National Black Student Debt Study, the report demonstrates that Black women borrow more for college while earning less, making repayment significantly more challenging than for other groups.

---

### 200. Making College Affordable

Type: report | Source: The Education Trust
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, edtrust
URL: https://edtrust.org/rti/making-college-affordable/

EdTrust advocates for reducing college costs and student debt through policy initiatives focused on highlighting affordability gaps in higher education, promoting free college programs, doubling Pell Grants, and addressing the disproportionate student debt burden faced by Black borrowers. The organization's goal is enabling students to earn degrees without it turning into a debt sentence, and this hub page links to related research, data tools, and advocacy resources on college affordability.

---

### 201. Evidence for ESSA: Reading Partners

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/reading-partners/

Reading Partners is a one-to-one tutoring program delivered by trained community volunteers who work with struggling readers in grades 2–5 for two 45-minute sessions per week. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on one MDRC randomized controlled trial (n=1,166) showing students gained significantly more on SAT-10 comprehension and other outcomes (effect size +0.10) compared to peers, two-thirds of whom received alternative literacy services.

---

### 202. Evidence for ESSA: Success for All

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, professional-development, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/success-for-all-whole-class/

Success for All is a comprehensive K–5 school reform program combining phonics instruction, cooperative learning, small-group tutoring, and frequent regrouping for high-poverty schools. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on six U.S. studies (n=8,849 students across 207 schools) including two RCTs, with an average effect size of +0.29 and particularly robust effects on foundational reading skills and for lower-achieving students.

---

### 203. Evidence for ESSA: Reading Recovery

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/reading-recovery/

Reading Recovery targets first-graders in the lowest 20–30% of their cohort, delivering daily 30-minute one-to-one lessons from specially trained teachers covering fluency, decoding, phonemic awareness, and guided reading. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on four qualifying studies (n=7,756 students) with an average effect size of +0.43 on standardized reading assessments including ITBS, Woodcock, and Gates measures.

---

### 204. Evidence for ESSA: Peer-Assisted Learning Strategies (PALS) — Reading

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/peer-assisted-learning-strategies-pals-reading-elementary-whole-class/

PALS is a peer-tutoring approach where first-grade student pairs alternate teacher and learner roles, working through a structured sequence of phonemic awareness, phonics, sound blending, and passage reading with error correction. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on three studies (n=1,501 students) with an average effect size of +0.23 on Woodcock reading scales.

---

### 205. Evidence for ESSA: Enhanced Core Reading Instruction (ECRI)

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, professional-development, response-to-intervention
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/enhanced-core-reading-instruction-ecri/

ECRI enhances Tier 2 supplemental reading instruction for struggling first graders by providing teacher professional development and small-group sessions (3–5 students) targeting phonemic awareness, decoding, fluency, and irregular word reading. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on one study (n=811 students in Oregon and Massachusetts) with an average effect size of +0.24 on Woodcock-Johnson and SAT-10 measures.

---

### 206. Evidence for ESSA: Reading Corps

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/reading-corps/

Reading Corps is an AmeriCorps program that places trained literacy tutors in K–3 classrooms to deliver 20-minute daily supplemental instruction using research-based protocols. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two RCTs (n=798 students in Minnesota and Wisconsin) with an average effect size of +0.36, with particularly strong gains in Letter Sound Fluency (+0.74) and Nonsense Word Fluency (+0.62) for K–1 students.

---

### 207. Evidence for ESSA: Targeted Reading Instruction (TRI)

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, coaching, computer-assisted-learning
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/targeted-reading-instruction-tri/

TRI is a one-to-one tutoring intervention that uses webcam technology to train educators to deliver 15-minute daily individualized reading sessions for struggling K–1 readers, covering oral language, decoding, writing, comprehension, vocabulary, and fluency. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two studies (n=471 students) with an average effect size of +0.51 on letter-word identification, word attack, and passage comprehension measures.

---

### 208. Evidence for ESSA: Sound Partners — Struggling Readers

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/sound-partners-struggling-readers/

Sound Partners is a one-on-one paraprofessional tutoring intervention for kindergarten and first-grade struggling readers, providing 30 minutes of daily instruction four days per week for 18–20 weeks in phonics, phonemic awareness, sight words, and decodable text reading. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two qualifying studies (n=488 students) with an average effect size of +0.58, with sustained gains confirmed at two-year follow-up assessments.

---

### 209. Evidence for ESSA: QuickReads — Struggling Readers

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/quickreads-struggling-readers/

QuickReads is a supplemental tutoring program for struggling readers in grades 2–5 that pairs students for 30-minute daily sessions four days per week over approximately 20 weeks, emphasizing repeated reading, phonics, and comprehension. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on three studies (n=483 students) with an average effect size of +0.21 on GORT and Woodcock reading assessments.

---

### 210. Evidence for ESSA: Air Reading

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, coaching, computer-assisted-learning
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/air-reading/

Air Reading is a virtual tutoring program for grades 1–6 that delivers explicit, skills-based reading instruction in small groups of up to four students meeting four times weekly for 30 minutes, with consistent tutors using diagnostic assessment to guide individualized instruction. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two RCTs (n=740 students in Texas and Louisiana) with a weighted average effect size of +0.20 across NWEA MAP, DIBELS, LEAP, and STAAR assessments.

### 211. Evidence for ESSA: Building Assets Reducing Risks (BARR) — Reading

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, professional-development
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/building-assets-reducing-risks-barr-reading/

BARR is a training and coaching model for K–12 schools built around structured teacher team meetings, data-driven student support, community engagement, and professional development to improve student outcomes. Evidence for ESSA rates the reading component Strong based on three randomized studies (n=9,398 students) with an average effect size of +0.08, with stronger impacts of +0.21 for struggling readers in high school settings.

### 212. Evidence for ESSA: Intelligent Tutoring for the Structure Strategy (ITSS)

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: literacy, k-12, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/intelligent-tutoring-for-the-structure-strategy-itss-secondary/

ITSS is a web-based intelligent tutoring system that teaches nonfiction text comprehension through text structure categorization, delivered in 30–45-minute weekly sessions in language arts classes with paraprofessional support. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on one RCT (n=2,489 seventh graders across 108 classrooms in 25 rural/suburban schools) with an effect size of +0.18 on the Gray Silent Reading Test after 6–7 months of use.

### 213. Evidence for ESSA: Zearn Math

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, personalized-learning
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/zearn-math/

Zearn Math is a nonprofit adaptive online supplement for K–8 math instruction featuring guided video lessons using a Concrete-to-Pictorial-to-Abstract progression with mastery-based quizzes. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on three studies (including one RCT with 10,000+ students in Texas) with an average effect size of +0.09 on NWEA MAP assessments, with strongest results when schools received dedicated implementation support including professional development and coaching.

### 214. Evidence for ESSA: ASSISTments

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, formative-assessment, automated-feedback
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/assistments/

ASSISTments is an online homework tool for grades 7–8 that provides students with math assistance during practice while giving teachers real-time assessment data on student progress. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two RCTs (a Maine study and a North Carolina replication with ~6,000 students) with a combined mean effect size of +0.13 on mathematics assessments.

### 215. Evidence for ESSA: DreamBox Math

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, personalized-learning, intelligent-tutoring
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/dreambox-learning/

DreamBox Math is an adaptive game-based online platform that delivers personalized, standards-aligned K–8 math instruction as a supplement to classroom teaching. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two RCTs (n=13,320 students in California and North Carolina) with an average effect size of +0.10 on the Number Knowledge Test and state assessments, with strongest impacts for K–2 students.

### 216. Evidence for ESSA: ST Math (Spatial Temporal Math)

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/st-math-spatial-temporal-math/

ST Math is a supplemental visual problem-solving program for grades 3–6 built on the science of how the brain learns, using animation and game-based tasks to develop mathematical understanding without language barriers. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on four studies (n=346,248 students) including two cluster-randomized trials in high-poverty schools, with an average effect size of +0.07 on state math assessments.

### 217. Evidence for ESSA: Math in Focus

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, professional-development, math-strategies
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/math-in-focus/

Math in Focus adapts Singapore's "My Pals Are Here! Maths" curriculum for grades 2–5 using a concrete-to-pictorial-to-abstract progression in carefully scaffolded lessons, supported by extensive professional development including summer training and four full-day sessions during the school year. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on four qualifying studies (n=3,444 students) with an average effect size of +0.15 on standardized math measures.

### 218. Evidence for ESSA: IXL Math

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, personalized-learning, formative-assessment
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/ixl-math/

IXL Math is a comprehensive personalized teaching and learning platform featuring adaptive skills practice aligned to state standards, video tutorials, diagnostic assessments, and analytics for monitoring progress at district, school, classroom, and individual levels. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on one cluster RCT (n=545 elementary students in Michigan) with an effect size of +0.13 on Renaissance Star Math, with particularly strong impacts for Grade 3, Hispanic, special education, and English learner subgroups.

### 219. Evidence for ESSA: Saga Math

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, coaching, computer-assisted-learning
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/saga-math/

Saga Math is a high-dosage tutoring intervention for grades 9–10 offering traditional (1:2–1:4) or technology-enhanced formats (1:8 alternating direct tutoring with ALEKS computer-assisted learning), delivered three times weekly for 90 minutes total to supplement regular math instruction. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on three studies (n=5,396+ predominantly Black and Latinx students in Chicago) with an average effect size of +0.14, plus increased math GPAs, reduced course failures, and persistent gains one to two years post-intervention.

---

### 220. Evidence for ESSA: Math Corps

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/math-corps/

Math Corps is a tutoring intervention for grades 4–8 where full-time AmeriCorps tutors provide approximately 25 students with 90 minutes of weekly intervention support in small sessions targeting foundational whole and rational number skills and algebraic reasoning. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two RCTs (n=1,164 students) with an average effect size of +0.16 on STAR Math and state assessments.

### 221. Evidence for ESSA: OGAP Math Professional Learning System

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, professional-development, formative-assessment
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/ogap-math-professional-learning-system-the-ongoing-assessment-project/

OGAP Math is a professional learning system for grades 3–5 teachers that develops mathematics content knowledge and formative assessment skills using research-based learning progressions, enabling teachers to analyze student work and identify strategies and misconceptions in real time. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on one two-year RCT (n=3,488 students across 61 urban schools near Philadelphia) with an effect size of +0.20 on Pennsylvania state math assessments.

### 222. Evidence for ESSA: Graspable Math — From Here to There (FH2T)

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, math-strategies
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/graspable-math-from-here-to-there-fh2t/

From Here to There (FH2T) is a digital math game for grade 7 in which students strengthen algebraic skills by dragging and transforming expressions using valid mathematical operations, practicing distribution, factoring, inverse operations, and order of operations. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on one study (n=1,119 seventh graders across 10 suburban middle schools) with an effect size of +0.14 on an algebraic understanding assessment after nine 30-minute sessions.

### 223. Evidence for ESSA: My Math Academy

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, early-childhood, prekindergarten, computer-assisted-learning, personalized-learning
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/my-math-academy/

My Math Academy is a game-based adaptive learning system for pre-K through 2nd grade featuring 30 games with 130+ activities, adaptive scaffolding, embedded assessment, and narrative-driven characters to build foundational number sense and operations. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two studies (n=1,209 students in Texas and Southern California) with an average effect size of +0.27 on CIRCLE and TEMA-3 math assessments.

### 224. Evidence for ESSA: Whole Number Foundations (Roots)

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, response-to-intervention
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/roots/

Whole Number Foundations is a Tier 2 supplemental intervention for kindergarten and first graders delivered by paraprofessionals in small groups of 1–5, with kindergarteners receiving 50 twenty-minute daily lessons and first graders receiving 60 sessions three to five times weekly targeting procedural fluency and conceptual understanding. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on five studies (n=2,140 students across Oregon, Massachusetts, Texas, and Boston) with an average effect size of +0.19 on SESAT and TEMA-3 measures.

### 225. Evidence for ESSA: Number Rockets

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, coaching
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/number-rockets/

Number Rockets is a scripted small-group tutoring intervention for first graders delivered by retired and substitute teachers in groups of 2–3 students for 40 minutes daily over 17 weeks, progressing from concrete to abstract mathematical tasks to build foundational number sense. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on one study (n=994 students below the 38th percentile) with an effect size of +0.34 on TEMA-3 assessments.

### 226. Evidence for ESSA: Fraction Face-Off!

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, coaching, math-strategies
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/fraction-face-off/

Fraction Face-Off! is a small-group tutoring intervention for at-risk fourth graders that delivers 35-minute daily sports-themed sessions over 12 weeks (36 days) focused on comparing, ordering, placing on number lines, and understanding equivalencies of fractions. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong based on two studies (n=425 students) with an average effect size of +0.51 on NAEP-derived fraction assessments.

### 227. Evidence for ESSA: Building Assets Reducing Risks (BARR) — Math

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: math-education, k-12, professional-development
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/building-assets-reducing-risks-barr-math/

BARR is a training and coaching model for K–12 schools that structures teacher team meetings around student relationship data and progress, supplemented by community engagement sessions and professional development, to improve academic outcomes. Evidence for ESSA rates the math component Strong based on three RCTs (n=9,386 students) with an average effect size of +0.09 on NWEA MAP and PSAT/NMSQT math assessments, with a +0.33 effect in one high school cohort.

### 228. Evidence for ESSA: Second Step — Social-Emotional Learning

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: sel, k-12
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/second-step-social-emotional-learning/

Second Step is a classroom-based SEL curriculum for K–7 that delivers 22–26 weekly lessons per year targeting social-emotional competence and self-regulation, with differentiated content for elementary (K–5) and middle school (6–7) students. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong in academic and emotional well-being categories based on six qualifying studies (n up to 7,213 elementary and 3,705 middle school students) showing effect sizes of +0.10–+0.11 on learning skills, emotional problems, and hyperactivity measures.

### 229. Evidence for ESSA: Facing History and Ourselves

Type: report | Source: Evidence for ESSA
Tags: sel, k-12, professional-development
URL: https://evidenceforessa.org/program/facing-history-and-ourselves/

Facing History and Ourselves provides teacher professional development that uses historical case studies addressing racism, prejudice, and antisemitism to promote students' humane and informed citizenship in grades 7–10. Evidence for ESSA rates it Strong in academic and social relationships categories based on three studies including one large RCT across 62 high schools showing effect sizes of +0.14 to +0.23 on historical understanding, tolerance, civic efficacy, civic engagement, and prosocial behaviors.

### 230. Principled Transformers for Predictive Performance in Knowledge Tracing

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/961

Introduces Knowledge Tracing Set Transformers (KTSTs), which apply transformer architecture with learnable ALiBi attention and set-based representations of learner interactions to forecast student capabilities over time. Evaluated on real educational datasets and simulated learning data, KTSTs establish improved benchmarks and are proposed as a simple but effective base model class for future knowledge tracing research.

---

### 231. Enhancing the De-identification of Personally Identifiable Information in Educational Data

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: pii-privacy, learning-engineering, nlp, jedm, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/936

Investigates GPT-4o-mini fine-tuning versus prompting for detecting personally identifiable information in educational text, benchmarking against Microsoft Presidio and Azure AI Language. The fine-tuned model achieved 0.9589 recall on the CRAPII dataset while reducing cost to roughly one-tenth of competing solutions, with consistent performance across demographic groups.

---

### 232. Deep Learning vs. Bayesian Knowledge Tracing: Student Models for Interventions

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/318

Compares Bayesian Knowledge Tracing, Intervention-BKT, and LSTM models on two prediction tasks using data from two intelligent tutoring systems. BKT variants outperformed LSTM on post-test score prediction, while LSTM excelled at predicting learning gains; the study also demonstrates that BKT can forecast post-test performance using only the earliest half of a student's training sequence.

---

### 233. The Continuous Hint Factory - Providing Hints in Vast and Sparsely Populated Edit Distance Spaces

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/158

Proposes the Continuous Hint Factory, an extension of the Hint Factory approach that generates next-step hints in sparse state spaces by averaging weighted reference states from past students rather than requiring exact matches. The framework applies Gaussian processes and edit distance theory, demonstrating improved accuracy in predicting student actions on open-ended programming tasks.

---

### 234. dAFM: Fusing Psychometric and Connectionist Modeling for Q-matrix Refinement

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, jedm, assistments
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/314

Presents dAFM, a model that merges psychometric Additive Factors Modeling with neural network backpropagation to refine Q-matrices—mappings between assessment items and knowledge components. Evaluated on Cognitive Tutor and ASSISTments datasets, models that refined expert-defined Q-matrices outperformed those learning from scratch, showing that combining expert knowledge with data-driven refinement improves generalization.

---

### 235. Decision Tree Modeling of Wheel-Spinning and Productive Persistence in Skill Builders

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, jedm, assistments
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/210

Uses decision tree classification on ASSISTments data to distinguish unproductive wheel-spinning from productive persistence in online math practice. The study identifies two student subgroups engaging in counterproductive help-seeking patterns and finds that spaced practice and limiting bottom-out hint use can reduce unproductive struggle and improve learning outcomes.

---

### 236. Who's Learning? Using Demographics in EDM Research

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, student-belonging, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/404

Surveys five years of EDM publications to examine how demographic variables—age, gender, race/ethnicity, SES, and geography—are reported and incorporated into analyses. Only 15% of studies actually used demographic data in models; the authors contextualize this within broader algorithmic bias concerns and call for more equitable and transparent reporting practices in educational data mining.

---

### 237. When is Deep Learning the Best Approach to Knowledge Tracing?

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring, computer-assisted-learning, jedm, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/451

Empirically compares logistic regression, deep learning, and Markov-based approaches to knowledge tracing across nine real-world datasets. Logistic regression with well-engineered features leads on moderate-sized datasets, while deep learning excels on large datasets where precise temporal information matters; the study also evaluates model calibration, an important consideration for real deployment.

---

### 238. Early Detection of Students at Risk - Predicting Student Dropouts Using Administrative Student Data from German Universities

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: dropout-prevention, higher-ed, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/389

Develops an early-warning system combining regression, neural networks, and decision trees via AdaBoost to predict student dropout from administrative records at two German universities. The model achieved 79–85% accuracy after one semester and 90–95% by the fourth semester, enabling institutions to target at-risk students with support before withdrawal becomes likely.

---

### 239. Using Demographic Data as Predictor Variables: a Questionable Choice

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, student-belonging, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/619

Examines the ethical and practical implications of including demographic variables as direct predictors in educational prediction models. The authors argue that using demographics as predictors can reinforce biases and reduce model utility, concluding that demographic variables yield greater fairness benefit when used to validate model equity rather than as predictive features.

---

### 240. Using Auxiliary Data to Boost Precision in the Analysis of A/B Tests on an Online Educational Platform

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: a-b-testing, learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms, jedm, assistments
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/646

Demonstrates how incorporating historical user data from machine learning models into A/B test analysis on ASSISTments can substantially improve precision without sacrificing statistical validity. Tested across 250+ randomized comparisons, the method provides precision gains equivalent to increasing sample size by 20% on average—and up to 50–80% in some cases—with additional benefits for subgroup analyses.

---

### 241. Tracing Systematic Errors to Personalize Recommendations in Single Digit Multiplication and Beyond

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: personalized-learning, math-education, k-12, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/382

Presents the Systematic Error Tracing (SET) model, which uses a bigraph linking errors to underlying causes—inspired by Ising model physics—to identify persistent mistake patterns in elementary multiplication. Applied to 25,000+ incorrect responses from 335 students on the Math Garden platform, SET outperforms baseline approaches for generating personalized learning recommendations.

---

### 242. Using a Latent Class Forest to Identify At-Risk Students in Higher Education

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: dropout-prevention, higher-ed, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/283

Introduces a latent class forest method—combining latent class analysis with random forest ensembles—to identify subgroups of academically vulnerable students in a large-enrollment introductory psychology course. The approach reveals key demographic and academic characteristics of at-risk students and evaluates how a peer-led Supplemental Instruction program performs across identified subgroups, enabling more targeted recruitment and support.

---

### 243. Statistical Consequences of using Multi-armed Bandits to Conduct Adaptive Educational Experiments

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: a-b-testing, learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/357

Uses simulation studies to investigate how multi-armed bandit (MAB) algorithms affect the statistical properties of adaptive educational experiments. MAB designs substantially improve student outcomes during an experiment but require roughly double the participants to maintain statistical validity and can increase false positive rates when student characteristics vary over time, highlighting a tradeoff between immediate student benefit and rigorous causal inference.

---

### 244. Analyzing Student Process Data in Game-Based Assessments with Bayesian Knowledge Tracing and Dynamic Bayesian Networks

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: computer-assisted-learning, intelligent-tutoring, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/397

Compares Bayesian Knowledge Tracing and Dynamic Bayesian Networks for analyzing student interaction data from Raging Skies, a game-based science assessment aligned to Canadian Grade 5 curriculum. The study evaluates both models on classification consistency and accuracy, contributing evidence on the viability of probabilistic knowledge models for formative game-based assessment.

### 245. Extending the Hint Factory for the Assistance Dilemma: A Novel, Data-driven HelpNeed Predictor for Proactive Problem-solving Help

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: intelligent-tutoring, learning-engineering, computer-assisted-learning, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/450

Extends the Hint Factory methodology to address the assistance dilemma by creating a data-driven HelpNeed classifier that identifies when students are on unproductive problem-solving paths in logic-based tasks. A controlled experiment showed that students receiving adaptive hints based on HelpNeed predictions achieved superior posttest outcomes, reduced help avoidance, and completed optimal solutions more efficiently than controls.

### 246. Adjusting the L Statistic when Self-Transitions are Excluded in Affect Dynamics

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, computer-assisted-learning, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/478

Identifies a systematic bias in the L statistic—a standard metric for measuring transitions between student affective states—when self-transitions are excluded from data. The authors propose L*, a corrected version that restores the chance value to zero, and validate it on both simulated affective sequences and real student data from digital learning environments.

### 247. Effects of Scenario-Based Assessment on Students' Writing Processes

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: writing-instruction, formative-assessment, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/443

Uses keystroke log analysis with a semi-Markov model to examine how scenario-based assessment design conditions—varying number of scenarios and task order—affect students' writing processes. A single-scenario with essay-last format produced fewer but longer editing phases and more fluid text generation, with findings grounded in cognitive writing theory and working memory constraints.

### 248. Optimizing Financial Aid Allocation to Improve Access and Affordability to Higher Education

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: college-access, higher-ed, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/609

Combines optimization algorithms with machine learning to guide merit and need-based financial aid allocation with student-centered affordability goals, moving beyond enrollment-focused institutional strategies. Analysis of admissions data identified seven budget-conscious allocation strategies capable of expanding enrollment access by over 100% while constraining budget growth below 7%.

### 249. Examining Algorithmic Fairness for First-Term College Grade Prediction Models Relying on Pre-matriculation Data

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: higher-ed, student-belonging, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/665

Builds a GPA forecasting model for first-semester students using only pre-college demographic and academic data, finding the model is less predictive for at-risk students than for majority counterparts. The study concludes that deploying prediction systems too early—before students have accumulated in-college behavioral data—may systematically disadvantage the very students who most need early support.

### 250. Multi-Dimensional Performance Analysis of Large Language Models for Classroom Discussion Assessment

URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/831

Evaluates LLM performance on scoring classroom discussion quality, examining how task formulation, context length, and few-shot examples affect accuracy, consistency, and computational efficiency. Using data from a randomized controlled trial, the best-performing LLM methods partially replicated human-scored results and successfully detected improvements in discussion quality over time.

### 251. Investigating Demographic Features and their Connection to Performance, Predictions, and Fairness in EDM Models

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: learning-engineering, student-belonging, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/718

Tests whether including demographic features actually improves predictive accuracy in four at-risk student datasets, finding that removing demographics rarely decreases performance but models still assign weight to them when available. The authors argue that accurate prediction is not always the right goal and advocate for causal understanding and context-specific evaluation of demographic features over blanket inclusion or exclusion.

### 252. A Scalable, Flexible, and Interpretable Analytic Pipeline for Stealth Assessment in Complex Digital Game-Based Learning Environments

URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/761

Proposes a stealth assessment pipeline combining machine learning with expert-designed features to evaluate multiple learning outcomes in Mission HydroSci, a 3D narrative educational game. The framework captures complex in-game behaviors, uses unsupervised dimensionality reduction, and applies Accumulated Local Effects visualizations for interpretability; code and sample datasets are publicly released to support generalizability.

### 253. Automated Feedback Generation for Student Project Reports: A Data-Driven Approach

Introduces Insta-Reviewer, a system that automatically generates instant feedback on student project reports using data-driven methods, filling a gap since prior automated feedback work focused only on simpler student work. A five-dimension evaluation framework shows that Insta-Reviewer achieves near-human quality feedback, though the authors also document obstacles remaining for practical deployment.

### 254. Optimizing Bayesian Knowledge Tracing with Neural Network Parameter Generation

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: intelligent-tutoring, learning-engineering, computer-assisted-learning, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/758

Proposes OptimNN and BKTransformer—two neural network approaches using hypernetworks and transformers respectively—to generate Bayesian Knowledge Tracing parameters that avoid suboptimal local minima. Both methods outperform existing BKT and deep knowledge tracing baselines while preserving BKT's interpretable skill-level estimates and student mastery probability outputs; implementation and datasets are publicly available.

### 255. CLST: Cold-Start Mitigation in Knowledge Tracing by Aligning a Generative Language Model as a Students' Knowledge Tracer

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: intelligent-tutoring, learning-engineering, llm-application, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/854

Addresses the cold-start problem in knowledge tracing by reformulating it as an NLP task and fine-tuning a generative LLM on formatted problem-solving datasets from math, social studies, and science. The framework achieves significantly enhanced prediction, reliability, and cross-domain generalization with fewer than 100 student records, demonstrating how LLM external knowledge can substitute for sparse interaction histories.

### 256. Developing a Feedback Taxonomy for Math: A Synergy of Perspectives through Data Mining Methods

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: automated-feedback, math-education, formative-assessment, learning-engineering, jedm, assistments
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/858

Develops an empirically grounded taxonomy for categorizing educator feedback on student math responses, using data mining to reconcile varying interpretations from both teaching professionals and researchers on an online math platform. The resulting shared language across stakeholders is designed to support scalable delivery of pedagogically meaningful feedback at scale.

### 257. Workload Overload? Late Enrollment Leads to Course Dropout

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: dropout-prevention, higher-ed, learning-engineering, jedm, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/826

Uses cross-lagged panel models on enrollment transaction data to establish a causal link between late course registration and subsequent course withdrawal, estimating the effect at approximately 0.8 standard deviations of additional drops per SD of delayed enrollment. About 17% of students enroll late and carry higher course loads, pointing to early planning interventions as a practical dropout-prevention strategy.

### 258. Using LLMs to Identify Indicators of Persistence from Students' Dialogues with a Pedagogical Agent

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Educational Data Mining
Tags: llm-application, nlp, english-learners, learning-engineering, jedm
URL: https://jedm.educationaldatamining.org/index.php/JEDM/article/view/1007

Investigates using ChatGPT4o with varying temperature settings to automatically code self-regulation indicators—including help-seeking, goal-setting, and self-efficacy—from over 10,000 chat turns by 107 English learner middle schoolers in a conversation-based math assessment. Self-efficacy showed the strongest human-LLM agreement; the study recommends deterministic settings for well-defined constructs and higher temperatures for theoretically ambiguous ones.

### 259. Exploring Fairness and Explainability in LLM-Generated Support for Online Learning Discussion Forums

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: learning-engineering, higher-ed, nlp, llm-application, genai, ai-ethics, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8885

Investigates how LLMs handle fairness and transparency when generating replies in online MOOC discussion forums, fine-tuning GPT-2, Gemma, and LLaMA on both standard and counterfactual datasets. The study introduces absolute distributional sentiment divergence to quantify demographic bias, finding that LLM-generated responses are generally more neutral than human replies but show varying bias patterns by gender. Counterfactual fine-tuning reduced bias and produced more balanced outputs, contributing practical methods for equitable AI support tools in educational environments.

### 260. Towards More Transparency in Learning Analytics: Sharing Information with University Students Increases Their Awareness of Data Collection Practices

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, pii-privacy, data-sharing, ai-ethics, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8713

Tests three data disclosure formats — generic text, detailed text, and an icon-based nutrition-label approach — to measure their effect on student understanding of learning analytics practices. Non-generic disclosures improved comprehension, though student acceptance of data collection and beliefs about sharing were unaffected by any disclosure format. The author concludes that institutions should revisit their data disclosure methods to ensure both accuracy and genuine transparency.

### 261. Balancing Act: Early, Fair, and Accurate Identification of At-Risk Students

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, computer-assisted-learning, personalized-learning, dropout-prevention, ai-ethics, formative-assessment, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8761

Develops fairness-aware machine learning models for identifying struggling students in Advanced Placement statistics, tested at three sequential course stages. By incorporating learning activity data and excluding sensitive demographic features, the models effectively identified at-risk learners at Stage 1 while maintaining equity across demographic groups. The authors evaluate multiple fairness mitigation techniques, offering practical recommendations for equitable early-warning systems in educational settings.

### 262. Use of Learning Analytics in K–12 Mathematics Education: Systematic Scoping Review of the Impact on Teaching and Learning

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: k-12, math-education, learning-engineering, meta-analysis, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8299

Systematic scoping review of 19 studies on learning analytics in K–12 mathematics, finding the field is emerging with applications across diverse curricula. Teaching approaches using analytics-informed data-based decision-making concentrate primarily on supervision and guidance, with generally favorable outcomes for student achievement and notably stronger benefits for higher-performing students. The authors introduce the concept of "guiding analytics for learners" as a framework for leveraging analytics to foster self-directed learning.

### 263. FATE in MMLA: A Student-Centred Exploration of Fairness, Accountability, Transparency, and Ethics in Multimodal Learning Analytics

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, learning-engineering, qualitative-research, ai-ethics, inclusive-design, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8351

Interviews 14 undergraduates who used multimodal learning analytics (MMLA) visualizations to reflect on collaborative learning activities, examining student perspectives on fairness, accountability, transparency, and ethics. Students emphasized that accurate and comprehensive data representation is essential for visualization fairness, and called for varied data access levels and continuous rather than one-time consent mechanisms. The authors conclude that the learning analytics community must systematically prioritize FATE concerns in system design.

### 264. Words of Wisdom: A Journey through the Realm of NLP for Learning Analytics — A Systematic Literature Review

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: learning-engineering, nlp, automated-feedback, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, writing-instruction, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8403

Analyzes 156 learning analytics papers applying natural language processing to educational contexts, finding that most work focuses on online discussion analysis and essay assessment. Key patterns: developed models are rarely tested in real settings, recent studies increasingly evaluate deep learning approaches such as BERT, datasets tend to be small and English-language, and average model performance reaches 0.54–0.79 on Cohen's Kappa and Accuracy. The review maps how NLP techniques extract insights from student essays, online discussions, and chat interactions.

---

### 265. Student Privacy and Learning Analytics: Investigating the Application of Privacy Within a Student Success Information System in Higher Education

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, pii-privacy, data-sharing, ai-ethics, qualitative-research, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/7975

Examines how privacy is operationalized in a commercial learning analytics system at a small public higher education institution using inductive coding of interviews, documents, and videos. The findings reveal an institution in the early stages of implementing such a system, with privacy handled reactively rather than proactively. The authors offer recommendations for institutions to adopt more proactive privacy measures when designing learning analytics policies.

### 266. Effectiveness of a Learning Analytics Dashboard for Increasing Student Engagement Levels

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, learning-engineering, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, personalized-learning, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/7935

Evaluates SensEnablr, a learning analytics dashboard integrating descriptive, predictive, and prescriptive analytics, finding that student engagement with learning technologies and course resources increased significantly following dashboard interactions. The tool elevated learner motivation and students valued predictive and prescriptive insights, addressing a gap in dashboards that typically provide only basic descriptive data. The study demonstrates that multi-analytic platforms can meaningfully impact student outcomes in tertiary online education.

### 267. Privacy in LA Research: Understanding the Field to Improve the Practice

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: learning-engineering, pii-privacy, data-sharing, ai-ethics, meta-analysis, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/7751

Scoping review of 59 learning analytics articles examining how privacy is conceptualized, finding that privacy was not defined at all in 74% of studies. Among the minority that did define it, frameworks included privacy as a right, state, control, or other approaches. The authors argue that poorly implemented privacy frameworks may undermine trust and call for the field to establish clearer privacy definitions to enable responsible practices around student data.

---

### 268. Causal Inference and Bias in Learning Analytics: A Primer on Pitfalls Using Directed Acyclic Graphs

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: learning-engineering, longitudinal, ai-ethics, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/7577

Introduces directed acyclic graphs (DAGs) as a practical tool for validating causal reasoning in learning analytics research, identifying three foundational pitfalls: confounding bias, overcontrol bias, and collider bias. The authors demonstrate how these methodological errors appear in published studies and propose DAG-based solutions for researchers working with observational data where randomized experiments are impractical. The paper emphasizes the importance of theoretical development alongside methodological rigor in the field.

---

### 269. A Participatory Approach to Designing a Student-Facing Dashboard for Online and Distance Education

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, learning-engineering, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, personalized-learning, inclusive-design, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8481

Engages 20 distance-learning students through screening questionnaires and focus groups to design student-facing analytics dashboards, finding students prioritize course support and communication with tutors and peers. Students valued descriptive metrics, predictive score forecasting, and prescriptive resource recommendations, with the study emphasizing that effective dashboards should foremost prescribe solutions to overcome performance challenges. The work demonstrates that participatory design approaches are essential for creating analytics tools that address genuine student needs.

### 270. Unveiling Accuracy-Fairness Trade-Offs: Investigating Machine Learning Models in Student Performance Prediction

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, learning-engineering, ai-ethics, digital-learning-platforms, personalized-learning, dropout-prevention, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8543

Analyzes the Open University Learning Analytics Dataset (OULAD) to evaluate accuracy-fairness trade-offs in machine learning models for student performance prediction. Standard ML models exhibit demographic bias, but applying bias mitigation techniques can reduce these disparities while maintaining acceptable accuracy. The authors conclude that auditing machine learning models for equitable performance across diverse student populations is essential before deployment.

### 271. The Coming but Uneven Storm: How AI Regulation Will Impact AI and Learning Analytics Research in Different Countries

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: learning-engineering, ai-policy, ai-ethics, data-sharing, pii-privacy, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8495

Analyzes 11 AI regulatory documents across geopolitical regions using the OECD classification system, finding that the EU and China have implemented the most comprehensive and strict AI regulations while the US shifted toward economic competition and reduced regulation. Regulatory priorities differ by region: the EU, UK, and China prioritize safety and bias prevention, while Japan and some African nations focus on economic potential; biometric data in educational contexts faces strict EU restrictions. The authors recommend researchers remain adaptable to evolving international regulations and use regulatory sandboxes to balance learner protection with developer flexibility.

### 272. Deliberative Interactions for Socially Shared Regulation in Collaborative Learning: An AI-Driven Learning Analytics Study

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, nlp, qualitative-research, computer-assisted-learning, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8393

Analyzes 2,125 utterances from video-recorded collaborative tasks involving 30 Finnish secondary students to examine socially shared regulation patterns. Two distinct deliberation patterns emerged: a Plan and Implementation Approach associated with adaptive group regulation, and a Trials and Failure Approach linked to maladaptive patterns, with many groups failing to recognize or respond to emerging regulatory needs. The study combines epistemic network analysis with multimodal data and AI-assisted coding, advancing understanding of how groups manage cognitive and emotional regulation during collaborative problem-solving.

### 273. Uncovering Engagement Profiles of Young Learners in K–8 Education through Learning Analytics

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms, personalized-learning, computer-assisted-learning, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8133

Applies k-means cluster analysis to e-learning trace data from grades 1–8 to identify seven distinct student engagement profiles, finding that some profiles were absent at specific grades, indicating shifting engagement behaviors across development. Younger students showed stronger interest in game-based learning components while middle school students prioritized exam preparation, and most students focused on particular platform features rather than using all available resources. The study generates seven design considerations for effective K–8 e-learning platforms.

### 274. Towards Data-Informed Teaching Practice: A Model for Integrating Analytics with Teacher Inquiry

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: learning-engineering, professional-development, formative-assessment, qualitative-research, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/7505

Develops and evaluates the Analytics Model for Teacher Inquiry (AMTI), examining teacher perspectives (N=10) on analytics-informed instructional decision-making including barriers and motivators. Data-informed decision-making implies deep practice change for many teachers, and the model was subsequently refined with feedback from specialists (N=7) and educator-researchers (N=2). The research generates example implementation scenarios for analytics-based teacher inquiry and contributes a practical framework for professional development.

### 275. Learning Analytics Dashboard Design and Evaluation to Support Student Self-Regulation of Study Behaviour

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, learning-engineering, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, personalized-learning, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8529

Uses a sequential mixed-methods design — focus groups, usability testing, and interviews — to develop and evaluate a study-behaviour dashboard for university students. Students and tutors agreed on the relevance of constructs from the literature but differed in ranking their importance, and the dashboard helped learners reflect on study patterns though the actual impact on behaviour varied. The authors recommend stronger integration between dashboards and existing educational practices to achieve greater effectiveness.

### 276. Advancing Multimodal Collaboration Analytics: A Scoping Review

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: learning-engineering, qualitative-research, meta-analysis, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8625

Reviews 36 empirical studies in multimodal collaboration analytics (MMCA), developing a definitional framework comprising five modality categories: auditory, visual, physiological, kinesthetic, and tactile. The study reveals that modality combinations in MMCA arise from technical, practical/pedagogical, methodological, or theoretical rationales, each contributing differently to insights about collaborative learning. The authors conclude that MMCA pursues comprehensive understanding of learner interactions during collaboration, moving beyond the constraints of analyzing individual data streams in isolation.

### 277. Developing a Stealth Assessment System Using a Continuous Conjunctive Model

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: math-education, k-12, computer-assisted-learning, formative-assessment, intelligent-tutoring, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/7639

Creates a mathematics educational game called The Nomads targeting rational number arithmetic and applies a continuous conjunctive model (CCM) for cognitive diagnostic assessment of player data. Unlike traditional diagnostic models, CCM generates parameters at the attribute level and offers more parsimonious diagnoses using continuous variables, lending itself well to the dynamic nature of game-based learning. Learners' attribute mastery improved during gameplay and learners benefited from scaffolding on three of the game's instructed attributes.

### 278. Network Analytics to Unveil Links of Learning Strategies, Time Management, and Academic Performance in a Flipped Classroom

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, learning-engineering, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, longitudinal, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/7843

Applies epistemic network analysis to trace data from 290 engineering students to examine relationships among learning strategies, time management, and academic outcomes in a flipped classroom. High-performing students effectively used their study time and enacted learning strategies linked mainly to formative and summative assessment tasks, while lower-performing students demonstrated less strategic variety and concentrated primarily on video consumption. The study provides actionable insights for flipped classroom design and data-informed instructional practice.

### 279. The Science Student Electronic Exit Ticket (SEET) System: Visualizations to Help Teachers Notice and Reflect on Classroom Inequalities

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, formative-assessment, professional-development, inclusive-design, ai-ethics, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8199

Evaluates the SEET system's equity analytics visualizations with 42 middle school science teachers across two groups in a two-month professional development program, using diary entries and interviews. Only equity visualizations — showing participation data disaggregated by gender and race/ethnicity — prompted teacher reflections on diverse student experiences, though teachers consistently rated whole-class visualizations as more practical to use. The study highlights a tension between equity-focused and usability-focused design priorities in teacher-facing learning analytics tools.

### 280. Interpreting Predictive Learning Sequences in a College Math Course through a Self-Regulated Learning Framework

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: higher-ed, math-education, learning-engineering, computer-assisted-learning, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, longitudinal, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8865

Collects multimodal data from 49 undergraduates completing a college math task — including digital interaction logs, think-aloud protocols, and self-reports — to validate which digital event sequences predict post-test performance. Sequences reflecting learner conscientiousness predicted better outcomes while sequences including video pausing and rewinding predicted poorer performance. The study provides validity evidence by aligning verbalizations with self-regulated learning processes captured in digital traces, though individual variability in the alignment calls for methodological refinement.

### 281. The Scope of Multimodal Learning Analytics in K–8: A Systematic Review

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, meta-analysis, digital-learning-platforms, pii-privacy, ai-ethics, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8505

Scoping review of 14 peer-reviewed empirical studies (2011–2023) on multimodal learning analytics in elementary K–8 education, finding varied applications but consistent gaps: studies rarely describe data fusion techniques or address ethics and transparency requirements. The review concludes that multimodal learning analytics holds promise for improving student outcomes but that the field requires more guidance and shared understanding for conducting rigorous work in K–8 contexts. Findings point to a need for clearer reporting standards and ethical frameworks tailored to young learners.

### 282. The Relationship between Wellbeing and Academic Achievement: A Comprehensive Cross-Sectional Analysis of System-Wide Data From 2016–2019

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, longitudinal, sel, formative-assessment, digital-learning-platforms, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8357

Analyzes Wellbeing Engagement Collection (WEC) index data from over 215,000 students in Years 4–10 across South Australia (2016–2019) to examine the relationship between wellbeing and academic outcomes. Learning readiness emerged as the most influential wellbeing component, with a more pronounced influence on male students particularly in literacy; effects were stable across year levels and time periods. The findings demonstrate learning analytics' potential for deepening system-level understanding of socio-emotional factors' relationship to academic success.

### 283. Learning Analytics in Schools: Is Digital Data Use Influenced by Teacher-Level or School-Level Factors?

Type: paper | Source: Journal of Learning Analytics
Tags: k-12, learning-engineering, professional-development, digital-learning-platforms, formative-assessment, qualitative-research, jla
URL: https://learning-analytics.info/index.php/JLA/article/view/8567

Surveys 2,247 teachers across 112 Swiss upper secondary schools to investigate what teacher-level and school-level factors drive educators' use of digital data for instructional decisions. Teacher-specific attributes — technology confidence, positive attitudes toward digital tools, and data access — significantly predict digital data use, while school-level factors such as collegial collaboration and principal support operated indirectly through individual teacher characteristics. The authors suggest findings can guide customized professional development strategies aligned with educator strengths and supportive institutional conditions.
