### 284. Targeted School-Based Interventions for Improving Reading and Mathematics for Students with or at Risk of Academic Difficulties in Grades K–6

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, literacy, meta-analysis, rct, response-to-intervention, personalized-learning
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/improving-reading-mathematics-academic-difficulties-grade-k-6

This 2021 Campbell systematic review synthesized 205 high-quality studies (607 total) examining school-based interventions for students with or at risk of academic difficulties in grades K–6. Peer-assisted instruction and small-group adult instruction showed the largest improvements in both reading and mathematics. Effects were positive in the short term with some fadeout but detectable gains up to two years post-intervention.

---

### 285. Targeted School-Based Interventions for Improving Reading and Mathematics for Students with or at Risk of Academic Difficulties in Grades 7–12

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, literacy, math-education, meta-analysis, rct, response-to-intervention
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/improving-reading-mathematics-academic-difficulties-grade-7-12

This 2020 Campbell systematic review examined 71 studies (52 RCTs) of school-based interventions for at-risk students in grades 7–12. Average effects on standardized reading and math tests were positive and statistically significant, with mathematics interventions showing larger effects than reading. Small-group instruction substantially outperformed computer-assisted instruction.

---

### 286. Mindfulness-Based Interventions for Improving Cognition, Academic Achievement, Behavior, and Socio-Emotional Functioning of Primary and Secondary Students

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, sel, qualitative-research
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/mindfulness-based-interventions-primary-and-secondary-school-students

This 2017 Campbell systematic review synthesized 35 randomized or quasi-experimental studies (6,207 participants) of school-based mindfulness interventions. MBIs produced small, statistically significant positive effects on cognitive and socioemotional outcomes, but not on behavioral or academic outcomes. The high risk of bias across included studies means further high-quality evidence is needed.

---

### 287. Effects of Trauma-Informed Approaches in Schools

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, sel, school-discipline
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/effects-of-trauma-informed-approaches-in-schools

This 2019 Campbell systematic review searched for studies of trauma-informed approaches in schools — programs integrating workforce development, trauma-focused services, and organizational environment changes — but found zero studies meeting inclusion criteria. Despite widespread adoption of trauma-informed practices in US and international schools, no rigorous evaluations had been conducted at the time of the review.

---

### 288. 21st Century Adaptive Teaching and Individualized Learning Operationalized as Specific Blends of Student-Centered Instructional Events

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, personalized-learning, intelligent-tutoring, learning-engineering
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/adaptive-teaching-individualized-learning-classroom-settings-k-12

This 2019 Campbell systematic review analyzed 299 studies (43,175 students, 2000–2017) comparing student-centered versus teacher-centered instruction in K–12. More student-centered conditions produced moderate positive effects on achievement; however, giving students excessive control over pacing showed a significantly negative relationship with outcomes. The combination of adaptability with a guiding teacher role produced the strongest effects.

---

### 289. The Relationship Between Homework Time and Academic Performance Among K-12: A Systematic Review

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, math-education, literacy
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/the-relationship-between-homework-time-and-academic-performance-among-k-12-a-systematic-review

This 2024 Campbell systematic review examined 11 experimental studies on homework effects for K–12 students. Homework showed a beneficial effect on primary school academic achievement, especially arithmetic computation and problem-solving. However, only one of the included studies was published after 1995, and the optimal duration of homework remains unclear, pointing to an urgent need for contemporary high-quality experiments.

---

### 290. Mobile Device Use in the Primary School Classroom and Impact on Pupil Literacy and Numeracy Attainment: A Systematic Review

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, digital-learning-platforms, computer-assisted-learning, literacy, math-education
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/mobile-device-use-in-the-primary-school-classroom-and-impact-on-pupil-literacy-and-numeracy-attainment-a-systematic-review

This 2024 Campbell systematic review examined 18 studies (11,126 participants) of tablets, smartphones, and handheld digital games in primary classrooms for children aged 4–12. Children using mobile devices showed better results on maths and literacy tests compared to control conditions, though study quality was mostly moderate-to-high risk of bias. Insufficient evidence exists to determine which device types or teaching strategies are most effective.

---

### 291. Montessori Education's Impact on Academic and Nonacademic Outcomes

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, early-childhood, meta-analysis, sel, personalized-learning
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/montessori-impact-on-academic-and-nonacademic-outcomes

This 2023 Campbell meta-analysis examined 32 rigorous studies (1970–2020) comparing Montessori to traditional education across preschool through high school in eight countries. Students in Montessori settings scored approximately 0.25 SD higher on academic outcomes and 0.33 SD higher on non-academic outcomes (executive function, well-being, social skills, creativity). Effects were strongest at preschool/elementary levels and in randomized studies.

---

### 292. Small Class Sizes for Improving Student Achievement in Primary and Secondary Schools

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, literacy, math-education
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/small-class-sizes-student-achievement-primary-and-secondary-schools

This 2018 Campbell systematic review examined 127 studies from 41 countries (10 in meta-analysis) on class size effects on academic achievement. The review concluded that small class sizes have at best a very small effect on reading and no significant effect on mathematics. Given the high cost of class size reduction and minimal demonstrated benefit, the authors emphasize the need for better evidence before resource allocation.

---

### 293. Later School Start Times for Supporting the Education, Health, and Well-Being of High School Students

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, longitudinal
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/later-school-start-times-education-health-well-being-high-school-students

This 2017 Campbell systematic review examined 17 reports of 11 interventions (297,994 participants across six countries) on delayed high school start times. Later start times appear to increase sleep, and some studies suggest positive associations with academic and psychosocial outcomes, but overall evidence quality is low and insufficient to draw firm conclusions. Possible adverse effects include reduced parent interaction and scheduling difficulties.

---

### 294. The Effectiveness of Volunteer Tutoring Programs

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, rct, literacy, coaching
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/effectiveness-of-volunteer-tutoring-programmes

This 2006 Campbell systematic review analyzed 28 study cohorts (1,676 participants, grades K–8) of volunteer tutoring programs in the USA. Programs showed positive effects on reading and language outcomes equivalent to approximately one-third of a standard deviation improvement (overall reading effect size: d = 0.23–0.30). Highly structured tutoring programs produced significantly greater effects than less structured approaches; reading comprehension and mathematics showed positive but non-significant trends.

---

### 295. Dropout Prevention and Intervention Programs: Effects on School Completion and Dropout Among School-Aged Children and Youth

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, dropout-prevention, longitudinal
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/dropout-prevention-intervention-programmes

This 2011 Campbell systematic review examined 548 reports describing 167 studies (1985–2010) of school and community-based dropout prevention programs. The review found that school dropout can be reduced through carefully implemented programs, but no single prevention or intervention strategy stood out as better than any other. Implementation quality and program intensity mattered more than the specific program type chosen.

---

### 296. Impacts of After-School Programs on Student Outcomes

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, rct, sel
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/impacts-of-after-school-programmes-on-student-outcomes

This 2006 Campbell systematic review examined five experimental studies of after-school programs combining academics with youth development and recreation activities. Programs did not contribute to higher reading achievement (d = 0.028, ns) or significant grade improvements, though they reduced unsupervised self-care by more than 0.5 SD and increased participation in enriching activities. Eighty-four percent of measured impacts showed no significant differences between program and control youth.

---

### 297. Approaches to Parent Involvement for Improving the Academic Performance of Elementary School-Aged Children

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, rct, professional-development
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/parent-involvement-improving-academic-performance-school-children

This 2006 Campbell systematic review found that parent involvement has a positive and significant effect on children's overall academic performance (overall d = 0.45; direct parent involvement programs d = 0.31). Benefits were observed even with a median intervention duration of only 11 weeks. The review provides support for parent involvement as a viable supplementary intervention, backing policies like the No Child Left Behind parent involvement mandate.

---

### 298. School-Based Interventions for Reducing Disciplinary School Exclusion

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, rct, school-discipline
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/reducing-school-exclusion-school-based-interventions

This 2018 Campbell systematic review examined 37 RCTs (mostly US and UK) of school-based interventions targeting exclusion rates in children aged 4–18. Interventions caused a small, significant drop in exclusion rates during the first six months, but effects did not sustain long-term, and no impact on antisocial behavior was detected. Academic skills enhancement, counselling, mentoring, and teacher skills training all showed some promise.

---

### 299. The 'Tools of the Mind' Curriculum for Improving Self-Regulation in Early Childhood

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: early-childhood, meta-analysis, rct, sel, prekindergarten
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/tools-of-the-mind-curriculum-self-regulation-early-childhood

This 2017 Campbell systematic review evaluated the Tools of the Mind early childhood curriculum across 14 records from 6 US studies. The curriculum showed statistically significant but small improvements in mathematics skills; improvements in self-regulation and literacy were not statistically significant. The evidence base is limited by the small number of included studies and methodological weaknesses, and more rigorous research on self-regulation outcomes is needed.

---

### 300. Preschool Predictors of Later Reading Comprehension Ability

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: early-childhood, literacy, meta-analysis, longitudinal, prekindergarten
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/preschool-predictors-of-later-reading-comprehension-ability

This 2017 Campbell systematic review examined 64 longitudinal studies (1986–2016) of preschool language skills as predictors of later reading comprehension. A broad set of language skills — both code-related (phoneme awareness, letter knowledge) and linguistic comprehension — are important for developing reading comprehension. The authors recommend that reading comprehension instruction target a broad set of language skills rather than focusing narrowly on decoding alone.

---

### 301. The Relationship Between Teacher Qualification and the Quality of the Early Childhood Care and Learning Environment

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: early-childhood, meta-analysis, professional-development, prekindergarten
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/teacher-qualification-and-quality-of-early-childhood-care-and-learning

This 2017 Campbell systematic review analyzed 48 studies with 82 independent samples on the relationship between teacher qualifications and early childhood education and care (ECEC) quality. Higher teacher qualifications are positively associated with higher overall quality in center-based ECEC settings, including program structure, language development, and reasoning skills. Because the evidence is correlational rather than causal, the authors recommend studies that can establish causal pathways through specific teacher competencies.

---

### 302. Indicated Truancy Interventions: Effects on School Attendance Among Chronic Truant Students

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, attendance, rct
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/truancy-interventions-effects-on-school-attendance

This 2012 Campbell systematic review examined 28 studies from the US, Canada, UK, and Australia (1,725 participants; 16 in meta-analysis) of truancy interventions for chronically absent students. Interventions were effective: treated students attended an average of 4.7 more school days than controls. No significant differences in effectiveness were found across different delivery channels or program formats, though attendance remained below acceptable levels in most cases.

---

### 303. The Effects of Teachers' Classroom Management Practices on Disruptive or Aggressive Student Behaviour

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, school-discipline, sel
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/classroom-management-effects-on-disruptive-aggressive-behaviour

This 2011 Campbell systematic review examined 12 studies of teacher classroom management practices in US and Dutch K–12 classrooms. Teachers' classroom management practices had a significant positive effect in decreasing aggressive or problematic student behavior across all included studies. However, the small sample sizes prevent definitive conclusions, and researchers could not identify which specific management components were most effective.

---

### 304. Service Learning for Improving Academic Success in Students in Grades K to 12

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, sel, student-belonging
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/service-learning-for-improving-academic-success-primary-and-secondary-students

This 2022 Campbell systematic review examined 10 US-based studies (over 8,000 participants) of school-based service learning — programs linking community service to academic instruction — in grades K–12. Evidence regarding academic success was inconclusive due to insufficient comparable studies, and no adverse effects were documented. The review is constrained to US contexts, limiting international generalizability.

---

### 305. Psychosocial Interventions for School Refusal with Primary and Secondary School Students

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, rct, attendance, sel
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/psychosocial-interventions-for-school-refusal

This 2015 Campbell systematic review examined 8 rigorous studies (435 participants, 1980–2013) of psychosocial interventions for school refusal in primary and secondary students. Cognitive-behavioral therapy (CBT) significantly increased school attendance but had no statistically significant effect on anxiety. Findings should be treated with caution due to unclear randomization in most studies and the small evidence base.

---

### 306. 'No Excuses' Charter Schools for Increasing Math and Literacy Achievement in Primary and Secondary Education

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, rct, math-education, literacy
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/charter-schools-maths-and-literacy-primary-and-secondary-education

This 2017 Campbell systematic review examined 18 US studies (5 RCTs, 13 quasi-experimental, 1990–2015) of 'No Excuses' charter schools, which combine high academic expectations, strict discipline, extended instruction time, and intensive teacher training. These schools are associated with greater student gains on standardized math and literacy measures than traditional public schools, with notably stronger effects in mathematics that grew over three years. Caution is warranted due to reliance on studies from a single charter management organization (KIPP).

---

### 307. Self-Management Interventions for Reducing Challenging Behaviors Among School-Age Students

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, sel, school-discipline, formative-assessment
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/self-management-interventions-school-student-behaviour

This 2022 Campbell systematic review analyzed 75 single-case design studies and 4 group-design studies of school-based self-management interventions for students with challenging behaviors. Interventions showed moderate effects for both behavioral and academic outcomes — including on-task behavior, prosocial behaviors, and work completion — with more meaningful effects for African-American students and students receiving special education services.

---

### 308. The Effect of Linguistic Comprehension Instruction on Generalized Language and Reading Comprehension Skills

Type: report | Source: Campbell Collaboration
Tags: k-12, early-childhood, literacy, meta-analysis, rct
URL: https://www.campbellcollaboration.org/review/linguistic-training-effect-on-language-and-reading-comprehension

This 2019 Campbell systematic review analyzed 43 studies (1992–2017) of linguistic comprehension interventions in preschool and school-aged children. Results showed a small positive immediate effect on generalized linguistic comprehension (vocabulary and grammar gains were small; narrative and listening comprehension gains were moderate), with negligible effects on reading comprehension. Programs appear insufficient to close vocabulary gaps, and preventing reading difficulties likely requires longer-term educational efforts.

---

### 309. Getting state 'free college' right: Design choices that matter

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, personalized-learning
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/getting-state-free-college-right-design-choices-that-matter/

This report examines state-level "free college" promise programs and finds they work best when "generous, easy to access, and paired with dedicated advising support." Although roughly one-third of first-year students attend college tuition-free, living expenses remain a heavy burden—low-income families spend about 38% of income on non-tuition costs after aid. The authors recommend states shift from last-dollar to first-dollar aid models and plan for federal funding volatility.

---

### 310. The complex ramifications of Students for Fair Admissions v. Harvard

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: higher-ed, k-12, longitudinal
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/the-complex-ramifications-of-students-for-fair-admissions-v-harvard/

This analysis documents a "cascade effect" following the 2023 Supreme Court ruling that ended race-conscious college admissions: underrepresented minority students displaced from elite institutions move to state flagships and less-selective schools, reshaping enrollment patterns across higher education. Black student enrollment has declined most sharply at elite colleges, and standardized testing policy significantly mediates diversity outcomes across institution types.

---

### 311. Rebuilding IES to amplify the impact of education research on student outcomes

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: learning-engineering, ai-policy, professional-development
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/rebuilding-ies-to-amplify-the-impact-of-education-research-on-student-outcomes/

This commentary argues for rebuilding the Institute of Education Sciences following roughly $1 billion in federal budget cuts, contending that "policymakers, practitioners, and education leaders value evidence" and need credible data to guide decisions. The authors propose three federal investment priorities: strengthening researcher-practitioner partnerships, funding implementation and cost studies, and maintaining rigorous, independent, publicly accessible research.

---

### 312. How immigration enforcement is harming US schools and students

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, english-learners, attendance, longitudinal
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/how-immigration-enforcement-is-harming-us-schools-and-students/

This article synthesizes research showing that intensified immigration enforcement correlates with increased chronic absenteeism, mental health deterioration, declining test scores, and reduced college enrollment rates among students from immigrant families, with particularly severe effects on Latino and English learner populations. The rescission of sanctuary protections for schools has left educators facing mounting pressures without adequate federal guidance or support systems.

---

### 314. Parents are not fully aware of, or concerned about, their children's school attendance

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, attendance, qualitative-research
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/parents-are-not-fully-aware-of-or-concerned-about-their-childrens-school-attendance/

This research finds that fewer than half of caregivers whose children are at risk of chronic absenteeism report being concerned about it, and reveals a significant gap between actual attendance data and parent-reported absences. Many parents view available online learning as offsetting the importance of in-person attendance, despite expressing belief that classroom presence matters—an attitude that may undermine post-pandemic recovery efforts.

---

### 315. School counselors are vital to navigating the FAFSA maze

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, professional-development
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/school-counselors-are-vital-to-navigating-the-fafsa-maze/

Examining the troubled rollout of the redesigned FAFSA, this piece presents research showing that adding school counselors significantly increases students' receipt of Pell grants and state scholarships. The author makes three recommendations: prioritize counselor time for FAFSA support, have states extend scholarship deadlines, and push college decision day back to June 1 to accommodate delays.

---

### 316. Career and technical education is a hidden weak spot in many high schools' teacher workforces

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, career-readiness, professional-development, longitudinal
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/career-and-technical-education-is-a-hidden-weak-spot-in-many-high-schools-teacher-workforces/

Using Tennessee data, this research finds that CTE teachers in high-growth occupational fields—IT, health sciences, and STEM—leave teaching at significantly higher rates than other educators, with departing instructors earning approximately 20% more in private sector roles. This turnover creates staffing challenges that sometimes result in fewer course offerings for students in career and technical programs.

---

### 317. Selective colleges and universities need to do more to enroll low-income students

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, personalized-learning
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/selective-colleges-and-universities-need-to-do-more-to-enroll-low-income-students/

This study evaluates the Advising Plus program, which used small financial incentives ($50–$100) to encourage low-income high school students to engage with remote college advisors. While the intervention successfully increased advising engagement and college applications, it "had no effect on whether or where students enrolled in college," suggesting behavioral nudges alone cannot overcome systemic admissions and affordability barriers at elite institutions.

---

### 318. Long-term solutions for college affordability require congressional and state action

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: higher-ed, college-access
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/long-term-solutions-for-college-affordability-require-congressional-and-state-action/

Analyzing student debt cancellation and FAFSA implementation, this piece argues that meaningful progress on college affordability requires legislative action from Congress and states—not executive initiatives operating within limited authority. The author uses both policy cases to demonstrate how legislative inaction forces executive branch workarounds that leave structural affordability problems unresolved.

---

### 320. Many high schools across the United States offer limited civics-focused extracurricular activities

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, qualitative-research
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/many-high-schools-across-the-united-states-offer-limited-civics-focused-extracurricular-activities/

Using a nationally representative survey of approximately 650 high school principals, this research finds that while 80% of schools offer student government, other civic activities—Model UN (19%), mock trials (26%)—remain rare. High-poverty schools provide substantially fewer civics opportunities than low-poverty schools, raising equity concerns about students' access to civic learning experiences that support democratic participation.

---

### 321. Early reading tests can aid educational recovery after the pandemic

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, literacy, formative-assessment, response-to-intervention
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/early-reading-tests-can-aid-educational-recovery-after-the-pandemic/

This study presents Virginia data showing that over one-quarter of kindergarten and first-grade students fell significantly behind in early reading skills in fall 2020—a 10-percentage-point increase from the prior year. The authors emphasize evidence-based interventions aligned with the science of reading to address emerging disparities and prevent long-term academic struggles.

---

### 322. School finance reforms made funding more equal by income, but not by race

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, longitudinal, meta-analysis
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/school-finance-reforms-made-funding-more-equal-by-income-but-not-by-race/

Analyzing state school finance reforms since 1990, this research finds that income-based reforms reduced funding disparities between low- and high-income districts by over $1,300 per pupil but "either did not change or widened funding gaps" between districts by racial composition, increasing racial funding inequalities by $740–$1,100 per pupil. The authors argue income-based policies alone cannot address racial disparities without considering school segregation patterns.

---

### 323. 2016 Brown Center Report on American Education: How Well Are American Students Learning?

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, math-education, literacy, formative-assessment, longitudinal
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/2016-brown-center-report-on-american-education-how-well-are-american-students-learning/

This flagship annual report covers three topics: Common Core implementation effects on math and reading instruction (finding no evidence that Common Core caused 2015 test score declines), whether eighth-grade math tracking correlates with AP success (states with more tracked classes produced more high-performing AP students across racial groups), and international variation in school principal leadership. The analysis concludes that high-performing countries show principals are reluctant to offer direct teaching advice.

---

### 324. The impact of COVID-19 on student achievement and what it may mean for educators

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, math-education, literacy, longitudinal, formative-assessment
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/the-impact-of-covid-19-on-student-achievement-and-what-it-may-mean-for-educators/

This study projects pandemic learning losses using historical test score data from millions of students, estimating that students could return to school in fall 2020 with roughly 70% of their prior-year reading gains and less than 50% of math gains. The authors also project increased variability in academic achievement levels, warning that equity gaps will widen across the student population.

---

### 325. The pandemic has had devastating impacts on learning. What will it take to help students catch up?

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, math-education, literacy, longitudinal, response-to-intervention
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/the-pandemic-has-had-devastating-impacts-on-learning-what-will-it-take-to-help-students-catch-up/

Measuring fall 2021 test scores for grades 3–8, this research found average math scores were 0.20–0.27 standard deviations below pre-pandemic levels, with reading also declining significantly. The study evaluates whether common recovery interventions—tutoring, summer programs, class-size reductions—are sufficient in scale and evidence base to close pandemic-era learning gaps, noting that equity disparities widened considerably during school closures.

---

### 326. A restorative approach to student discipline shows promise in reducing suspensions and arrests

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, school-discipline, rct, longitudinal
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/a-restorative-approach-to-student-discipline-shows-promise-in-reducing-suspensions-and-arrests/

Examining Chicago Public Schools' implementation of restorative practices, this research finds that the program reduced student suspension days by 18% in the four years after rollout, with Black students experiencing double the average reductions. The study provides causal evidence that restorative approaches—emphasizing dialogue and harm reparation over punishment—can meaningfully reduce disciplinary disparities.

---

### 327. Reclassifying English Language Learners: What's the effect on Wisconsin high schoolers?

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, english-learners, longitudinal, college-access
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/reclassifying-english-language-learners-whats-the-effect-on-wisconsin-high-schoolers/

This study finds that reclassifying English Language Learners as fully proficient during high school increases composite ACT scores by about one full point and boosts postsecondary enrollment, particularly at four-year institutions. The results suggest schools should ensure equitable access to college preparation resources for students scoring near proficiency reclassification thresholds.

---

### 328. Do teacher expectations matter?

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, longitudinal, qualitative-research
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/do-teacher-expectations-matter/

Analyzing nationally representative data from approximately 6,000 tenth-grade students, this research provides causal evidence that teacher expectations directly affect students' long-term educational attainment. The authors also document that white teachers hold systematically lower expectations for Black students compared to Black teachers, and that this racial bias in expectations has measurable negative effects on Black students' college completion rates.

---

### 329. How does student-teacher matching affect suspensions for students of color?

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, school-discipline, longitudinal
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/how-does-student-teacher-matching-affect-suspensions-for-students-of-color/

Using 10 years of New York City public school data, this study finds that Black, Latino, and Asian American students experience fewer suspensions when assigned to teachers of the same racial or ethnic background. The authors estimate that increasing teacher diversity could prevent thousands of student suspensions annually and keep students in classrooms for thousands more instructional days over a decade.

---

### 330. High school computer science impacts college majors and increases earnings

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, higher-ed, career-readiness, longitudinal, computer-assisted-learning
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/high-school-computer-science-impacts-colleg-majors-and-increases-earnings/

Using Maryland longitudinal data, this research finds that taking a high school computer science course leads to a five-percentage-point increase in students' likelihood of earning a bachelor's degree in CS and improves employment outcomes. Benefits are particularly pronounced for historically underrepresented groups, though these same students show lower enrollment rates when CS courses become available—pointing to access and encouragement gaps.

---

### 332. Special education: Beneficial to many, harmful to others

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, longitudinal, inclusive-design
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/special-education-beneficial-to-some-harmful-to-others/

Examining a 2005 Texas policy capping special education enrollment, this research finds that students who genuinely need special education services benefit significantly from them, while those inappropriately placed experience worse long-term educational outcomes. Notably, reducing racial disproportionality in placement improved outcomes for Black students, suggesting some were previously misclassified into special education rather than supported through general education.

---

### 333. Class size: What research says and what it means for state policy

Type: report | Source: Brookings Institution
Tags: k-12, meta-analysis, early-childhood
URL: https://www.brookings.edu/articles/class-size-what-research-says-and-what-it-means-for-state-policy/

This review of empirical literature finds that reductions of 7–10 fewer students per class can produce meaningful academic gains, particularly for disadvantaged elementary students, but that the magnitude of effect varies considerably across studies and grade levels. The authors conclude that policymakers must weigh class-size reduction against other evidence-based educational investments given the substantial and ongoing fiscal costs involved.

---

### 334. Examining Implementation and Outcomes of the Project On-Track High-Dosage Tutoring Program

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: literacy, k-12, professional-development, coaching
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/examining-implementation-and-outcomes-project-track-high-dosage-tutoring-program

REL Appalachia (REL 2024-005) examined how northeastern Tennessee school districts implemented the Niswonger Foundation's Project On-Track literacy tutoring initiative for early elementary students. The program uses Amplify Reading to group students by skill level and generate mini-lessons aligned to the science of reading. After one year, 42% of students who started as most at-risk improved to lower risk categories; rural schools heavily favored in-school delivery (92%) compared to non-rural schools (47%).

---

### 335. Effectiveness of Early Literacy Instruction: Summary of 20 Years of Research

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: literacy, k-12, early-childhood, meta-analysis
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/systematic-literature-review/effectiveness-early-literacy-instruction-summary-20-years-research

REL Southeast (REL 2021-084) synthesized over 74,000 studies published between 1997 and 2017, ultimately identifying 132 evidence-based early literacy interventions across 109 high-quality experimental and quasi-experimental studies. The review found that domain-specific instruction reliably increases performance in that domain, and that combined phonological awareness and print knowledge instruction shows promise for improving decoding and early writing skills. Language-focused instruction was found to be more effective in small group or one-on-one settings.

---

### 336. Developing a Measure of Middle School Math Teachers' Pedagogical Content Knowledge for Computational Thinking

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: math-education, k-12, professional-development, formative-assessment
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/developing-measure-middle-school-math-teachers-pedagogical-content-knowledge-computational-thinking

REL Midwest (REL 2026-007) developed and validated the CT-PCK Survey, a brief instrument measuring middle school teachers' ability to integrate computational thinking into mathematics instruction. Teachers scored approximately 61% correct on average, with those holding traditional certifications and those with five or more years of experience performing significantly higher. The survey is designed for use in professional development evaluation and institutional needs assessment in Midwest urban schools facing declining math achievement.

---

### 337. A Pilot Study of Write to Succeed: An Intervention to Enhancing Writing Instruction in New Mexico

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: literacy, k-12, english-learners, professional-development, writing-instruction
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/pilot-study-write-succeed-intervention-enhancing-writing-instruction-new-mexico

REL Southwest (REL 2025-013) evaluated the Write to Succeed professional learning program in partnership with the New Mexico Public Education Department. The pilot involved 22 teachers across five schools in three districts during the 2023-24 school year, with a focus on scaffolded writing instruction that embeds supports for English learner students. Data collected via coach logs, teacher surveys, and interviews provided the New Mexico PED with implementation evidence for potential expansion.

---

### 338. California's Special Education Local Plan Areas: Funding Patterns, Inclusion Rates, and Student Outcomes

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, qualitative-research, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/californias-special-education-local-plan-areas-funding-patterns-inclusion-rates-and-student-outcomes

REL West (REL 2022-134) analyzed 2016-17 data on California's Special Education Local Plan Areas (SELPAs), examining how funding configurations, inclusion rates, and student outcomes vary across SELPA types. The authors recommend that California investigate which regionalized special education programs benefit students in small districts and gather additional data to support more complex analyses of outcomes attributable to specific SELPA configurations.

### 339. Implementation of Career- and College-Ready Requirements for High School Graduation in Washington

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, career-readiness, college-access, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/implementation-career-and-college-ready-requirements-high-school-graduation-washington

REL Northwest (REL 2020-020) examined Washington state's 2014 legislation requiring 24 credits for high school graduation, finding that district implementation grew from 9% for the class of 2018 to 56% for the class of 2019. Only 27% of 2018 graduates statewide met all requirements, with significant gaps among economically disadvantaged students, English learners, and students of color. Increased credit requirements showed minimal impact on student academic outcomes between 2013 and 2018.

---

### 340. Additional Certification for Teachers in New York State: Teachers' Experience and Employment Location, Certification Pathways, and Certification Areas

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, professional-development, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/additional-certification-teachers-new-york-state-teachers-experience-and-employment-location

REL Northeast & Islands (REL 2022-110) studied how New York State teachers with at least one year of experience obtained additional certificates between October 2015 and October 2017. Approximately 5% earned additional certificates during the period; more teachers earned certificates in shortage areas than non-shortage areas, with special education as the most frequently pursued area. Teachers obtaining additional certificates were less experienced on average than those who did not, and over half used traditional in-state certification pathways.

---

### 341. Examining the Mentoring Experiences of First-Year Teachers in Missouri

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, professional-development, coaching, qualitative-research
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/examining-mentoring-experiences-first-year-teachers-missouri

REL Central (REL 2025-014) examined the frequency, duration, activities, and topics of mentoring received by a sample of first-year teachers in Missouri to provide the state Department of Elementary and Secondary Education with data for strengthening its mentoring initiative. The research used descriptive statistics to analyze mentoring patterns, supporting Missouri's goal of improving new teacher retention through evidence-informed program design.

---

### 342. Stabilizing School Performance Indicators in New Jersey to Reduce the Effect of Random Error

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, formative-assessment, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/stabilizing-school-performance-indicators-new-jersey-reduce-effect-random-error

REL Mid-Atlantic (REL 2025-009) tested Bayesian hierarchical modeling as a method to reduce the impact of random error on school accountability indicators in New Jersey, particularly for smaller student groups. Stabilization substantially improved reliability for test-based indicators such as proficiency rates and median student growth percentiles, and led to meaningful changes in which schools were designated for support and improvement. Non-test-based indicators such as chronic absenteeism and graduation rates proved less amenable to the approach.

---

### 343. Examining the English Language Arts Course Placement System at the College of the Marshall Islands

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: higher-ed, english-learners, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/examining-english-language-arts-course-placement-system-college-marshall-islands

REL Pacific (REL 2026-006) evaluated a 2021-22 revision to the College of the Marshall Islands' ELA placement system that added a multiple-choice test and a writing component alongside high school GPA. Only 11% of first-time students placed into credit-bearing ELA courses under the new system compared to 22% previously; students in intensive pathways of credit-bearing courses showed the highest passing rates. The writing component did not predict any outcomes, leading the authors to recommend CMI consider removing it and weighting high school GPA more heavily.

---

### 344. Evidence and Gap Map of Tier 2 Literacy Interventions for Grades K–3 in the Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: literacy, k-12, early-childhood, meta-analysis
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/rel/Products/Region/pacific/Publication/108204

REL Pacific (REL 2025-007) conducted a systematic review of supplemental literacy programs for K–3 students in the Northern Mariana Islands, where in 2019 only 24% of grade 3 students were reading at or above grade level. Of 267 relevant studies identified, 20 met rigorous quality standards; two interventions — Reading Recovery and Literacy First — demonstrated strong evidence under ESSA standards, and Achieve3000 showed moderate evidence. The report includes an evidence gap map and a matrix documenting implementation strategies for each reviewed intervention.

---

### 345. Teaching Fractions Toolkit

Type: framework | Source: IES Regional Education Labs

REL Midwest developed this professional development toolkit in partnership with the Illinois State Board of Education to help grade 6 math teachers implement evidence-based practices for teaching fractions and rational number computation. Grounded in the WWC practice guide Developing Effective Fractions Instruction for Kindergarten Through 8th Grade, the toolkit includes teacher professional development materials, resources for instructional leaders, and supplemental training for state, regional, and district leaders. The initiative aims to strengthen students' conceptual understanding of fractions, ratios, and rates with particular focus on closing achievement gaps.

### 346. Strategies to Improve Reading

Type: framework | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: literacy, k-12, early-childhood, professional-development, coaching

REL Midwest partnered with Michigan school districts to develop and implement the STIR (Strategies to Improve Reading) approach for grades K–2 literacy instruction, focusing on phonological awareness and phonics practices that help students decode unfamiliar words. The initiative builds educator capacity across three areas: effective instructional practices, data-driven decision-making, and leadership support. Resources, tools, trainings, and coaching are provided to help teachers implement and refine evidence-based early literacy routines.

### 347. A Toolkit to Support Evidence-Based Writing Instruction in Grades 2 Through 4

REL Mid-Atlantic created this free professional development toolkit comprising eight one-hour professional learning community sessions designed for grades 2–4 teachers, school leaders, and PD coaches. Built on the WWC What Works Clearinghouse practice guide on writing instruction and informed by practitioners from four Washington, D.C. charter schools, the toolkit provides a facilitator's guide, teacher's guide, instructional videos, lesson plans, and a school leader's guide. ### 348. Toolkit to Support Evidence-Based Algebra Instruction in Middle and High School

Type: framework | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: math-education, k-12, professional-development, math-strategies, formative-assessment
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/ncee/rel/algebra-middle-and-high-school/intro

REL Central developed this professional development toolkit to help algebra educators implement evidence-based recommendations from the WWC practice guide on improving algebra knowledge in middle and high school students. The toolkit organizes resources around three recommendations — using solved problems, teaching students to recognize algebraic structure, and selecting appropriate solution strategies — and uses a Professional Learning Community model with Plan-Do-Study-Act cycles to lower the barrier to implementation. It includes facilitator guides, participant workbooks, data collection tools, and videos for use by individual educators or school teams.

### 349. REL Northwest's Guide to Community Engagement Data Collection and Analysis

Tags: k-12, qualitative-research, professional-development
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/resource/other-resource/rel-northwests-guide-community-engagement-data-collection-and-analysis

REL Northwest published this 2026 guide to help education agency staff collect, analyze, and act on community engagement input from students, families, educators, and community partners. The guide provides 12 supporting resources organized across three phases — before, during, and after engagement — including ready-to-use checklists, tip sheets, and templates for research question design, note-taking, codebook generation, data analysis, and findings dissemination. It emphasizes that agencies that demonstrate genuine responsiveness to community feedback build trust and improve program quality.

### 350. Exploring Implementation of Trauma-Engaged Practices in Alaska Schools

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, sel, qualitative-research, student-belonging
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/exploring-implementation-trauma-engaged-practices-alaska-schools

REL Northwest (REL 2025-011) examined how Alaska schools implement trauma-engaged practices using the state's Transforming Schools Framework, drawing on administrative data and surveys. Most schools were at an emerging implementation level; schools with higher awareness of state support resources showed substantially higher implementation. Implementation levels predicted student perceptions on two school climate measures — Caring Others and Cultural Connectedness — but did not significantly affect other measured outcomes. School leaders identified staff buy-in, professional development, dedicated funding, and community partnerships as critical success factors.

### 351. Applying a Cycle of Evidence-Based Continuous Improvement When Selecting Interventions and Project Components to Improve Attendance

Type: framework | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, attendance, formative-assessment
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/resource/fact-sheetinfographicfaq/applying-cycle-evidence-based-continuous-improvement-when-selecting-interventions-project

REL West published this December 2023 fact sheet presenting an overview and worked example of how districts can apply a continuous improvement cycle when selecting attendance interventions or project components to reduce chronic absence. The resource addresses how to identify root causes of absenteeism, select appropriate evidence-based supports, and monitor implementation effectiveness using a structured, data-informed approach. It is designed for district and school leaders working to address chronic absence, which affects approximately 14.8 million students nationwide.

### 352. Principal Retention Patterns in Arizona, Nevada, and Utah

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, longitudinal, professional-development
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/principal-retention-patterns-arizona-nevada-and-utah

REL West (REL 2021-129) examined principal retention across Arizona, Nevada, and Utah, finding that fewer than half of principals in each state remained at the same school over the four-year period from fall 2016 to fall 2020. Retention rates varied significantly by school performance level, with substantially lower retention at lower-performing schools. When principals left their positions, those who remained in the profession tended to transfer within the same school district rather than to a different district.

---

### 353. Student Group Differences in Arkansas' Indicators of Postsecondary Readiness and Success

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, higher-ed, college-access, career-readiness, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/student-group-differences-arkansas-indicators-postsecondary-readiness-and-success

REL Southwest (REL 2023-145) analyzed middle and high school indicators predicting postsecondary success in Arkansas using data from grade 6 cohorts from 2008/09–2009/10, examining variation by race/ethnicity, economic status, disability status, and other characteristics. Indicator attainment varied substantially across student groups, with the largest differences between students with and without a designated disability; academic indicators showed greater disparities than behavioral ones. Predictive accuracy of indicators remained largely consistent across demographic groups, though specific indicators — notably ELA and science proficiency in middle school — showed variation in predictive strength for some populations.

---

### 354. English Language Development Among American Indian English Learner Students in New Mexico

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, english-learners, longitudinal, early-childhood
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/english-language-development-american-indian-english-learner-students-new-mexico

REL Southwest (REL 2022-135) tracked two cohorts of American Indian English learner students who entered kindergarten in 2013/14 or 2014/15 in New Mexico public schools, examining English proficiency progress over five years. The majority were not reclassified as English proficient within the state's ESSA-aligned five-year goal timeframe, and most did not meet grade-level standards in ELA and math in grades 3 and 4. Students attending a bilingual multicultural education program for at least four years showed higher reclassification and academic achievement rates than peers without such exposure.

---

### 355. An Examination of the Costs of Texas Community Colleges

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: higher-ed, college-access, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/examination-costs-texas-community-colleges

REL Southwest (REL 2023-142) examined whether Texas community colleges have sufficient funding to help all students meet performance-based milestones, using needs analysis, equity analysis, and cost function analysis. Colleges serving higher proportions of first-generation, economically disadvantaged, academically disadvantaged, older, and English learner students earned fewer success point milestones per full-time equivalent student. Current spending levels were found to be insufficient to cover the cost of providing equal opportunity to disadvantaged student populations to achieve outcomes comparable to their peers.

---

### 356. Exploring Implementation of Attendance Supports to Reduce Chronic Absenteeism in the Providence Public School District

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: k-12, attendance, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/report/descriptive-study/exploring-implementation-attendance-supports-reduce-chronic-absenteeism-providence-public-school

REL Northeast & Islands (REL 2021-099) examined attendance support initiatives in Providence Public School District during 2018–19, identifying which supports were most effective at reducing chronic absenteeism. Schools experiencing decreased chronic absenteeism implemented text messaging, phone calls, and mentorship programs with greater fidelity; multilingual text outreach showed particular promise in reaching families. Schools with declining absenteeism rates adopted attendance-related text messaging faster than schools where absenteeism increased.

### 357. Ask an Expert: College- and Career-Readiness Interventions

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs

REL Appalachia (published June 2022) compiled this resource identifying 15 college and career readiness interventions that meet ESSA Tier 1, 2, or 3 evidence standards, with particular attention to whether research was conducted in rural areas or with economically disadvantaged students. The resource provides details on each intervention's evidence tier, research context, and outcome domain, helping practitioners in REL Appalachia's region select evidence-based approaches suited to their specific student populations and geographic contexts.

### 358. High-Quality Early Child Education is Associated With Outcomes

Type: report | Source: IES Regional Education Labs
Tags: early-childhood, k-12, prekindergarten, longitudinal
URL: https://ies.ed.gov/use-work/resource-library/resource/fact-sheetinfographicfaq/high-quality-early-child-education-associated

REL West published this November 2025 infographic summarizing research-identified outcomes associated with high-quality early childhood education across four domains: kindergarten readiness, educational progress, long-term outcomes including college enrollment and employment, and health benefits. The summary identifies four essential features of high-quality programs: evidence-based curricula with play-based instruction and teacher coaching; educators with bachelor's degrees and K–12 equivalent compensation; small class sizes with low staff-to-child ratios; and full-day formats. Disadvantaged populations — including low-income children and children of color — were found to benefit most substantially.

REL Pacific (REL 2025-008, December 2024) examined how long teacher education students take to complete associate's degree programs at Palau Community College, prompted by Public Law 10-32 requiring all teachers to obtain an associate's degree in education or their subject area by end of 2023. The study aimed to support policymakers in understanding teacher certification timelines and help education leaders in Palau develop evidence-based strategies for training, retaining, and recruiting qualified educators across the Pacific region.

### 366. Operationalizing AI in K-12 Education: Five District Use Cases

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, genai, ai-policy, ai-ethics, professional-development, personalized-learning, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/01088747-6290-416c-a3be-ffbd9f7ca286

Developed through the U-GAIN Reading R&D Center, this report translates five critical EdTech recommendations into practical district use cases for building capacity, ensuring governance, and maintaining instructional integrity. Drawing on examples from three districts—Orcutt Union, Indian Prairie, and Allentown—the report illustrates how to build collaborative networks, develop cross-functional procurement teams, tailor professional learning, set guardrails, and establish AI-specific accountability systems. ### 367. Research and Development in America's Schools

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, professional-development, digital-learning-platforms, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/f5c1ea09-7178-44de-bd85-758eb9a45332

This report examines how school systems build and implement research and development (R&D) to drive sustainable improvement and innovation, drawing on direct work with schools and a national landscape analysis. It includes tools for school systems to assess their R&D practices and provides recommendations for deepening the use of R&D to accelerate innovation. The report highlights the conditions, practices, and real-world examples that enable system-level R&D grounded in evidence and local context.

### 368. How R&D Infrastructure for Postsecondary Education Could Unlock New Advances

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: higher-ed, digital-learning-platforms, pii-privacy, data-sharing, open-datasets, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/3c8445b8-2cbd-4079-b1b0-b3896b8b3a22

This paper articulates a vision for a modern postsecondary R&D infrastructure to overcome systemic barriers—including faculty autonomy, non-standardized assessments, and siloed student data—that impede large-scale instructional innovation. Examining initiatives within the SEERNet research network, including Arizona State University's Learning@Scale data warehouse and the Terracotta and OpenStax Kinetic experimental tools, the author demonstrates how integrated datasets and open-access instruments can lower barriers to rigorous experimentation. The paper calls for an ethos of openness and public investment in research infrastructure to prevent privatization of educational insights.

### 369. Privacy Enhancing Technologies in Digital Learning Platforms

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: pii-privacy, data-sharing, digital-learning-platforms, higher-ed, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/07793ba3-13f3-48cb-932e-c77cd9b524f7

This report argues that Privacy Enhancing Technologies (PETs)—including encryption, differential privacy, and synthetic data—should be treated as core research infrastructure for digital learning platforms, functioning as both technical tools and social technologies for responsible data governance. PETs allow valuable analyses such as securely linking education and workforce records or comparing outcomes across sites, while meeting the ethical obligation to protect students, many of whom are minors. The paper is part of the SEERNet initiative's work on building trustworthy research infrastructure for educational platforms.

### 370. What States Say about Evaluating AI in Education

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, ai-policy, genai, digital-learning-platforms, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/e7134e28-9fb9-4087-8e5f-b6e39651d81d

This report examines state-level AI in education evaluation guidance across 32 U.S. states and Puerto Rico, categorizing state AI guidance across three developmental stages: Nascent & Exploratory, Emergent & Piloting, and Systematic & Evidentiary. Findings show a majority of states engaged in exploratory activities with few conducting systematic, large-scale assessment of AI-enabled edtech's impact on student learning outcomes. The report provides recommendations for progressing through evaluation stages and integrating co-design feedback loop processes into evaluation activities.

### 371. Promoting Mathematical Reasoning in OpenSciEd Middle School Curriculum Units

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, math-education, math-strategies, professional-development, formative-assessment, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/4ea4b3c5-c663-4484-8727-258bff346d2d

This study responds to the need to support science teachers in deepening students' engagement in mathematical reasoning, collaborating with two districts to explore integration of mathematics into middle school science classrooms using OpenSciEd instructional materials. The research team designed professional learning experiences and resources to help teachers deepen their mathematics knowledge, support students' mathematical reasoning, and modify instructional materials to enhance connections to mathematics. Findings indicate that teachers can enhance student engagement in mathematics during phenomenon-based science instruction given appropriate resources and support.

### 372. AI Literacy in PK-12 Education

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, early-childhood, genai, ai-policy, professional-development, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/19fd2afb-0811-4e48-90d9-0ad6c9887a1a

This brief (part of a set sharing AI literacy recommendations for various educational audiences) provides guidance to make progress in PK-12 AI literacy implementation, which has gained widespread support at national, state, and local levels with momentum building across computer science courses and interdisciplinary integrations. It recommends a flexible, multi-level approach that reflects the need for AI literacy guidance to be adaptable across learning contexts rather than prescribing specific tools or methods. The brief is designed to support educational leaders and policymakers in developing AI literacy policies and pathways.

---

### 373. AI Literacy in Postsecondary Education

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: higher-ed, genai, ai-policy, professional-development, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/428af7f6-6c95-422e-8914-e420023aca46

This brief (part of a set sharing AI literacy recommendations for various educational audiences) outlines foundational AI skills and competencies for postsecondary educators and learners alongside key gaps in AI literacy for these groups. It suggests recommendations for reducing AI literacy gaps in the postsecondary setting, including establishing comprehensive institutional AI governance frameworks while implementing and sustaining context-specific educator development and support programs. The brief is focused on providing actionable guidance to postsecondary educational leaders and policymakers.

### 374. Integrating AI-Enabled EdTech in PK16 Education: Five Recommendations

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, higher-ed, genai, ai-policy, ai-ethics, professional-development, personalized-learning, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/92bbf863-78fd-4652-bfc0-d34c9cecdb39

This brief provides five actionable recommendations for state, district, and local leaders to guide the responsible integration of AI-enabled educational technologies across PK-16 systems, warning that without careful planning, governance, and investment, AI tools risk widening equity gaps and undermining trust. The recommendations focus on collaborative adoption, transparent governance, professional learning, classroom integration, and accountability systems. The brief aims to ensure AI-enabled edtech strengthens teaching and learning while safeguarding learners and supporting equitable access to future-ready opportunities.

### 375. AI-Enabled Edtech Adoption Cycle

Type: framework | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, higher-ed, genai, ai-policy, digital-learning-platforms, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/ee9d7371-1891-4e8e-b27b-57be24bba9a9

The AI-enabled edtech adoption cycle presents four interconnected phases—Vision and Planning, Implementation, Ongoing Evaluation, and Vision and Planning—emphasizing that AI-enabled EdTech adoption is not a linear process but an ongoing cycle of improvement. The framework requires intentional planning, collaboration, and commitment to data-driven refinement throughout each phase. By integrating these considerations, institutions can more effectively leverage AI technologies to enhance teaching and learning outcomes while ensuring sustainable, equitable implementation.

### 376. A Framework for Powerful Learning with Emerging Technology

Type: framework | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: learning-engineering, genai, personalized-learning, digital-learning-platforms, inclusive-design, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/fd21576c-7fe8-45fe-af18-b92536d5a704

This framework puts forward research-based, field-informed guidelines for designing and implementing emerging technology tools in ways that are evidence-based, learner-centered, and skill-building, developed through interviews with more than 50 experts, collaboration with a working group of 10 distinguished professionals, and a literature review. It considers both the opportunities and challenges that come with emerging technologies, offering guidance to education leaders, educators, learners, and edtech developers. The framework identifies key principles, practices, and strategies to support powerful learning through emerging technology.

### 377. Researching Digital Learning Platforms: Foundations, Methods, and Policy Recommendations

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms, data-sharing, ai-policy, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/aafb2b73-681e-4752-ba89-831298968061

This working paper observes that educational research on technology has been accelerating rapidly but that platform data is most often used only minimally as a measure of usage or dosage, while a smaller subfield dives more deeply into digital learning platform (DLP) data streams. It gives examples of three types of theories connected to DLP data, illustrates the range of rigorous methods that have been successfully employed, and addresses emerging work on using DLP data to study responsible AI use. The authors recommend bringing attention to the DLP-as-research-infrastructure movement as a distinct and growing subfield that can produce actionable insights for product developers, education leaders, and educators.

### 378. A National Context of Generative AI for Reading to Support English Learners

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: english-learners, literacy, genai, genai-tutoring, personalized-learning, pii-privacy, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/73c883c0-4652-499d-aeb2-74f773749c60

This U-GAIN Reading R&D Center report investigates generative AI applications for enhancing reading instruction to achieve equitable gains for diverse elementary students, including English Learners, combining an edtech market scan with interviews and listening sessions involving 16 educators across 11 states. Findings indicate that districts prioritize the Science of Reading and that edtech platforms show a trend toward integrating social-emotional learning, personalized tutoring, and real-time assessments. Key opportunities include customizing texts to student interests and reading levels and facilitating adaptive activities, but concerns emerged about AI biases, Automated Speech Recognition inaccuracies for diverse speech patterns, and student data privacy.

### 379. Glossary of Artificial Intelligence Terms for Educators

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, genai, ai-policy, professional-development, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/ed330bf1-6697-4cb7-9189-79eba8eb0a1e

This bilingual (English and Spanish) resource serves as an essential reference guide for educators learning about and implementing AI systems and tools, providing clear, accessible definitions of key AI concepts including algorithms, machine learning, and neural networks. The glossary maintains a focus on learning applications and addresses critical considerations such as bias in training data, interpretable machine learning, and human-centered approaches to AI implementation. It was authored with collaboration from Fundación Universitaria del Área Andina and emphasizes the importance of maintaining human agency in learning settings, advocating for AI as a tool to augment rather than replace teachers.

### 380. Unlocking the Potential of Technology Innovations: A Vision for Supporting Multilingual Learners

Tags: english-learners, early-childhood, digital-learning-platforms, inclusive-design, digital-promise

This report presents a landscape study examining how technology and digital media are currently leveraged to support young multilingual learners (MLLs) ages 3–8, combining a comprehensive research literature review, an exploratory resource landscape scan, and interviews with leading educational technology and digital media designers and researchers. The study recognizes multilingualism as an asset and documents a need and opportunity for research and development efforts to center MLLs and ensure digital tools are designed to effectively support their learning. Findings inform design and research recommendations for future efforts aimed at creating edtech with and for MLLs.

### 381. From Here to There (FH2T): Educator Perceptions of Game-Based Algebraic Learning

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, math-education, computer-assisted-learning, math-strategies, professional-development, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/7dcf9d16-b5ad-4067-be9f-be30319b1185

Building on prior efficacy research, Digital Promise facilitated a Research-Practice-Industry Partnership (RPIP) and confirmatory study to explore the usability, feasibility, and scalability of the FH2T game-based algebra tool, bringing together algebra educators, product developers from Graspable Math, and learning scientists. The research goal was to understand how FH2T could be implemented at scale and how digital tools can be used to democratize complex mathematical concepts for students. The project employed professional learning, co-design, and research activities to ensure each group's voice was heard and power dynamics were ameliorated.

### 382. Portraits in Progress: Emerging Future-Ready Skills Assessment Strategies

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, formative-assessment, career-readiness, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/0a2c7a9e-634b-4ec1-ba5d-3c8bfa19e696

As schools, districts, and states establish Portraits of a Graduate, this report details assessment strategies being used to assess future-ready skills—including performance-based assessments, defenses of learning, and badging—finding that districts prioritize student-centered assessments emphasizing growth, self-evaluation, and feedback. The authors recommend that districts clarify their purpose for future-ready skills assessment and align their assessment system with their instructional vision. Policy recommendations include investing in research to create reliable and valid tools for assessing future-ready skills and aligning recognition systems across K–12, postsecondary education, and the workforce.

### 383. Expected and Emerging Requirements for Digital Learning Platforms as Research Infrastructure

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: digital-learning-platforms, data-sharing, pii-privacy, learning-engineering, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/d1e385e3-78d6-4a6b-bc21-f802e156c12d

This white paper examines progress made by digital learning platforms (DLPs) in the SEERNet initiative—funded by the Institute of Education Sciences—which aims to advance research infrastructure by bridging the gap between practice and research. Expected requirements addressed include enhancing platform data capabilities, enabling experimental research designs, and protecting data privacy, while emerging needs included standardized workflows, researcher outreach strategies, and templates for IRB approvals and data-sharing agreements. The paper reflects on lessons learned from SEERNet's efforts, highlighting innovations in data documentation, experimental workflows, and collaborative relationship building.

### 384. Connecting SEERNet and Improvement Science to Pursue Better Outcomes in Schools

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms, english-learners, data-sharing, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/5999568b-65a0-414c-86dc-2f392ce5996f

This white paper explores how SEERNet—a network of digital learning platforms, researchers, and educators—can be integrated with Improvement Science methodologies to rapidly test and scale solutions for student learning challenges. It examines the collaborative power of Networked Improvement Communities (NICs) and illustrates through a scenario how a school district could use iterative Plan-Do-Study-Act (PDSA) cycles to address reading comprehension barriers in STEM subjects for English learners and students with disabilities. The paper concludes with five recommendations: fostering collaboration, enhancing data sharing, leveraging root cause analysis, implementing iterative improvements, and scaling successful interventions.

### 385. Practitioner-reported Needs for Enacting, Implementing, and Adopting OpenSciEd Curriculum Materials

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, professional-development, formative-assessment, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/bb9a5f32-e4b6-4489-a5e6-ccc2348a4a27

This report identifies OpenSciEd practitioners' most urgent needs through survey responses from 155 teachers and leaders and focus group interviews with 28 respondents, finding three broad challenge areas related to district adoption and implementation, classroom enactment and engagement, and obtaining evidence of NGSS-based student outcomes. Seven themes emerged for supporting practitioners through research, development, and innovation, with professional learning and other supports for teachers appearing to address root causes of many challenges. The report provides direction to researchers, practitioners, policymakers, and developers on how OpenSciEd-enabled research could drive system-level change in science education.

### 386. Social Regulation of Learning

Type: report | Source: Digital Promise
Tags: k-12, sel, formative-assessment, digital-promise
URL: https://digitalpromise.dspacedirect.org/items/c522759d-e6a8-41f0-9e6d-c4881558f931

This primer explores social regulation of learning as a critical component of successful collaborative learning, encompassing self-regulation, co-regulation, and socially shared regulation of learning, and discusses how these components help students navigate social, cognitive, and emotional challenges within collaborative settings. The primer highlights the teacher's role in fostering regulation skills, the importance of a positive classroom climate, and the need for students to be given time in groups without their teacher to develop shared regulation skills. It provides practical indicators and strategies for educators to enhance collaborative learning experiences, integrating newer research through the eyes of practitioners and researchers working toward deeper understanding and application.
