### 459. Adapterrex — Erroneous Examples Studies (2011–2019)

Type: dataset | Source: Carnegie Mellon University LearnLab
Tags: open-datasets, learning-engineering, math-education, k-12, intelligent-tutoring, a-b-testing, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=495

A public collection of 10 datasets from the Adapterrex project, contributed by PI Bruce McLaren (CMU), investigating the learning benefits of erroneous examples versus conventional problem-solving in middle-school mathematics. Studies ran from Fall 2011 through Spring 2019 across multiple school sites (Hopewell, Steel Valley, and others), with transaction counts ranging from approximately 4,300 to 376,000 per dataset. The research used randomized controlled designs (ErrEx vs. PS conditions) to examine whether studying worked examples containing deliberate errors improves conceptual understanding and transfer. DataShop IDs 495, 534, 579, 586, 592, 659, 1307, 2223, 2648, 2996. Listed as a public project.

---

### 460. Blocked vs. Interleaved Instruction — Fraction Arithmetic

Type: dataset | Source: Carnegie Mellon University LearnLab
Tags: open-datasets, learning-engineering, math-education, k-12, a-b-testing, intelligent-tutoring, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=1190

A public PSLC DataShop dataset contributed by PI Rony Patel examining the effects of blocked versus interleaved practice on fraction arithmetic (addition and multiplication) learning. Two datasets are available: DS1190 (Fraction Addition and Multiplication, April 2015–August 2016, ~24,453 transactions) and DS1706 (Blocked vs. Interleaved condition comparison, August 2016–March 2018, ~365,312 transactions). Subject area: Math/Other. The datasets support analysis of how the sequencing of different problem types during practice affects learning outcomes, a topic with strong relevance to instructional design and spacing/interleaving research.

---

### 461. iSnap — Introductory Programming (2015–2018)

Type: dataset | Source: Carnegie Mellon University LearnLab
Tags: open-datasets, learning-engineering, computer-assisted-learning, higher-ed, k-12, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=1920

A public collection of seven datasets capturing students' block-based programming interactions with iSnap, a logging-enabled fork of the Snap! visual programming environment, contributed by PI Thomas Price (NC State University). Data spans Fall 2015 through Spring 2018 (DataShop IDs 1920, 1921, 1922, 2517, 2724, 2738, 5667) with per-semester transaction counts ranging from approximately 84,000 to 208,000. iSnap records detailed step-by-step programming actions — code edits, hint requests, and project states — enabling fine-grained analysis of novice programming behavior, hint-seeking strategies, and knowledge component modeling for introductory CS education. Listed as a public project on DataShop.

---

### 462. Virginia Tech OpenDSA — Formal Languages eTextbook (Fall 2019)

Type: dataset | Source: Carnegie Mellon University LearnLab
Tags: open-datasets, learning-engineering, higher-ed, computer-assisted-learning, digital-learning-platforms, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=3427

A public PSLC DataShop dataset contributed by PI Cliff Shaffer (Virginia Tech) recording student engagement with the OpenDSA open-source interactive eTextbook covering Formal Languages during Fall 2019. OpenDSA delivers algorithm and data-structures content through embedded visualizations, exercises, and automated feedback. The dataset captures student interaction logs from a deployed university course, supporting research on self-paced eTextbook usage, exercise completion patterns, and learning from interactive educational resources. Subject area: Computer Science/Other. Listed as a public project (DataShop ID 3427).

---

### 463. Pavlik — Knowledge Tracking: Chinese Vocabulary Studies (2006–2007)

Type: dataset | Source: Carnegie Mellon University LearnLab
Tags: open-datasets, learning-engineering, higher-ed, computer-assisted-learning, longitudinal, cmu-learnlab
URL: https://pslcdatashop.web.cmu.edu/DatasetInfo?datasetId=107

A public collection of eight datasets from the Pavlik Knowledge Tracking project, contributed by PI Phil Pavlik (University of Memphis, formerly CMU), capturing students' Chinese vocabulary and character learning in computer-assisted language practice sessions. Datasets span Spring 2006 through Fall 2007 and include studies of vocabulary scheduling, Chinese radical transfer, and pinyin learning (DataShop IDs 107, 108, 115, 160, 161, 212, 213, 2745). Subject areas: Language/Chinese, Language/Other. Transaction counts range from tens of thousands to over 100,000 per dataset. The studies informed the development of the ACT-R–based spacing algorithm used in Pavlik's knowledge tracing and memory models. Listed as a public project on DataShop.

---

### 464. Education at a Glance (EAG)

Type: dataset | Source: OECD
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, early-childhood
URL: https://www.oecd.org/en/publications/serials/education-at-a-glance_g1gha6b0.html

Education at a Glance is OECD's authoritative annual statistical compendium on education systems worldwide, published each September. Each edition provides more than 100 internationally harmonised indicators covering the output of educational institutions; the impact of learning on earnings and employment; access, participation, and progression through education levels; financial resources invested in education; and teachers, learning environments, and school organisation. Data are drawn from the joint UNESCO-OECD-Eurostat (UOE) administrative data collection and from OECD's own surveys (PISA, TALIS, PIAAC), and cover OECD member countries plus a range of partner economies. The 2025 edition (released September 2025, 542 pages) is the most recent. Researchers use EAG as the primary cross-national reference for structural and system-level education indicators.

---

### 465. PISA for Development (PISA-D)

Type: dataset | Source: OECD
Tags: open-datasets, k-12
URL: https://www.oecd.org/en/data/datasets/pisa-d-pisa-for-development.html

PISA for Development (PISA-D) is an adapted version of the PISA assessment designed to support low- and middle-income countries in using internationally comparable assessment data to monitor progress toward national targets and SDG 4. PISA-D uses the same proficiency scales as standard PISA but adds more granular performance descriptors at the lower end of the scale, enhanced questionnaire instruments relevant to developing-country contexts, and — uniquely — an out-of-school component assessing 14–16-year-olds who are not enrolled. Nine countries participated in the school-based assessment (Bhutan, Cambodia, Ecuador, Guatemala, Honduras, Paraguay, Senegal, Zambia); five conducted the out-of-school assessment (Guatemala, Honduras, Panama, Paraguay, Senegal). School-based results were released December 2018; out-of-school results in 2020. Public-use files in SAS and SPSS formats are freely downloadable and include student, principal, teacher, parent, and out-of-school respondent records, codebooks, questionnaires, and data compendia.

---

### 466. TALIS Starting Strong

Type: dataset | Source: OECD
Tags: open-datasets, early-childhood, professional-development
URL: https://www.oecd.org/en/data/datasets/TALIS-Starting-Strong-Database.html

TALIS Starting Strong is an international large-scale survey of staff and leaders in early childhood education and care (ECEC), conducted under the OECD Teaching and Learning International Survey programme. Its goal is to generate robust internationally comparable data on the ECEC workforce to inform policy on staff working conditions, professional development, pedagogical practices and beliefs, well-being, job satisfaction, and intent to remain in the profession. The survey also addresses diversity in ECEC settings, use of digital technologies, and leadership practices. The 2024 cycle collected data from approximately 17 countries and subnational entities; an earlier 2018 cycle is also available. Public-use files in CSV, Rds, and SPSS formats are downloadable for both cycles, alongside questionnaires, conceptual frameworks, technical reports, and user guides. The dataset is closely related to TALIS (which covers primary and secondary teachers) but focuses exclusively on ECEC settings.

---

### 467. Survey on Social and Emotional Skills (SSES)

Type: dataset | Source: OECD
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, formative-assessment
URL: https://www.oecd.org/en/about/programmes/oecd-survey-on-social-and-emotional-skills.html

The OECD Survey on Social and Emotional Skills (SSES) is the largest global initiative to gather comparable cross-national data on the social and emotional skill development of 10- and 15-year-old students. The survey measures a broad set of skills organised into five domains: task performance (persistence, responsibility, self-control, achievement motivation), emotional regulation (stress resistance, emotional control, optimism), engaging with others (assertiveness, sociability, energy), open-mindedness (curiosity, creativity, tolerance), and collaboration. Contextual data are collected from students, teachers, school principals, and (optionally) parents. Round 1 (2019) covered 10 cities/regions; Round 2 (2023) expanded to 16 sites across six countries and ten sub-national entities — including Bulgaria, Chile, Peru, Spain, Mexico, Ukraine, and cities in Colombia, India, UAE, Italy, Japan, Finland, China, Indonesia, and Brazil — surveying approximately 18,000 ten-year-olds and 52,000 fifteen-year-olds. Datasets for both rounds are available on request from OECD. The SSES 2023 database page and 2019 database page provide application and access details.

---

### 468. OECD Online Education Database (UOE)

Type: dataset | Source: OECD
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed
URL: https://search.oecd.org/education/database.htm

The OECD Online Education Database is the annual administrative data collection underpinning Education at a Glance indicators. Conducted jointly by OECD, the UNESCO Institute for Statistics, and Eurostat (the UOE joint data collection), it has run in its current form since 1993. The collection comprises approximately 25 electronic questionnaires covering student enrolments (nine questionnaires), student entrants (four), graduates (three), personnel (three), education finance (three), class sizes (two), and general population data (one). Data are reported by Ministries of Education or national statistical offices according to international standards and the ISCED classification. Indicators derived from UOE cover educational outputs, access, participation and progression, human and financial resources invested in education, and structural features of national education systems. Raw UOE data are available through the OECD Education data portal and through the OECD.Stat platform; methodological guidance is provided in the UOE Data Collection Manual.

---

### 469. IDEA Section 618 Data

Type: dataset | Source: U.S. Department of Education
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, early-childhood
URL: https://www.ed.gov/data/idea-section-618-data

The IDEA Section 618 Data portal collects and publishes annual data on children and youth with disabilities receiving federally mandated special education services under the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act (IDEA). Coverage spans infants and toddlers (birth through age 2) served under Part C early intervention programs, and children ages 3–21 served under Part B special education programs. A searchable database allows users to retrieve state-submitted datasets by year and category; additional data notes and downloadable products are linked to ED's Open Data Platform at data.ed.gov.

---

### 470. National Training, Education, and Workforce Survey (NTEWS)

Type: dataset | Source: National Center for Education Statistics (NCES)
Tags: open-datasets, higher-ed, career-readiness, longitudinal
URL: https://nces.ed.gov/surveys/ntews/

NTEWS is a biennial household survey co-sponsored by NCES and the National Science Foundation's National Center for Science and Engineering Statistics (NCSES), administered by the U.S. Census Bureau. It collects data on educational enrollment and attainment, nondegree credential types, work experience programs (apprenticeships and internships), employment characteristics, and demographic characteristics, with particular emphasis on the Skilled Technical Workforce — individuals with advanced science and engineering skills but no bachelor's degree. The pilot phase launched in 2022 targeting adults ages 16–75, with the next collection planned for spring 2024; pilot estimates are designated experimental statistics pending quality review.

---

### 471. Condition of Education

Type: dataset | Source: National Center for Education Statistics (NCES)
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, early-childhood
URL: https://nces.ed.gov/programs/coe

The Condition of Education is NCES's flagship annual report presenting key education indicators across all levels of the U.S. system, from early childhood through postsecondary education and into the labor market. The 2024 edition covers six major topic areas — family characteristics, elementary and secondary education, postsecondary enrollment and outcomes, employment and earnings by educational attainment, international comparisons, and school crime and safety — with data updated throughout the year as new sources become available. Indicators are accessible as interactive web pages organized by topic and demographic subgroup, with PDF archives dating back to 1989.

---

### 472. Digest of Education Statistics

Type: dataset | Source: National Center for Education Statistics (NCES)
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, early-childhood
URL: https://nces.ed.gov/programs/digest/

The Digest of Education Statistics is an annual NCES compendium spanning the full breadth of American education from prekindergarten through graduate school. It aggregates data from both government and private sources on schools, colleges, teachers, enrollments, graduates, educational attainment, finances, and federal funding, supplemented by population trends, labor force characteristics, and international comparisons. Current tables and historical versions are available online back to 1995, with PDF archives from 1990–2020; a new Digest State Dashboard provides state-level interactive profiles for all 50 states, D.C., territories, and the Bureau of Indian Education.

---

### 473. Education Recovery Project — COVID Learning Loss Data

Type: dataset | Source: Stanford CEPA
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, longitudinal
URL: https://edopportunity.org/recovery/data

A national dataset tracking pandemic-related learning loss and recovery across U.S. school districts in reading and math from 2019 to 2024, released by Stanford's Educational Opportunity Project (SEDA 2024.2, updated February 2026). As of spring 2024, U.S. students remained nearly half a grade level behind pre-pandemic achievement in both subjects; the data also captures the impact of remote learning policies and federal pandemic relief funding on district-level recovery trajectories. Download requires a data use agreement; raw files are available for independent analysis alongside an interactive district-level explorer.

---

### 474. Segregation Tracking Project — School and Neighborhood Segregation Data

Type: dataset | Source: Stanford CEPA
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, longitudinal
URL: https://edopportunity.org/segregation/data

A multi-decade dataset tracking racial/ethnic and economic segregation across U.S. schools and neighborhoods, available at the state, county, metropolitan area, and school-district level (version 2.0, updated February 2026). Underlying research analyzes patterns from 1991 to 2020 and finds that school segregation has increased over the past three decades, particularly in large urban districts, driven substantially by policy choices. Raw data are downloadable under a data use agreement alongside an interactive mapping explorer and peer-reviewed methods documentation.

---

### 475. District Court Order Desegregation Data

Type: dataset | Source: Stanford CEPA
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, longitudinal
URL: https://cepa.stanford.edu/data/district-court-order-data

A dataset cataloging all medium-to-large U.S. school districts ever placed under a court-ordered desegregation plan, covering 358 court cases affecting 850 school districts plus 207 HEW actions since 1978. Each record includes case name, state, NCES district ID, year of initial case, current plan status, and dismissal date; data were compiled from case dockets, Department of Justice records, NAACP Legal Defense materials, and U.S. Department of Education files and verified against Westlaw. Available in Stata (versions 12 and 15), Excel, SAS 7, and SPSS formats; last updated February 2021 with revised dismissal statuses.

---

### 476. Opportunity Atlas — Neighborhood-Level Economic Mobility Data

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, longitudinal, college-access
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/the-opportunity-atlas/

A publicly available dataset built from anonymized longitudinal records covering nearly the entire U.S. population, tracking outcomes for children from the 1984–1989 birth cohorts (measured at approximately age 35) by Census tract, county, commuting zone, and national level. Measures include household income, incarceration rates, and neighborhood characteristics, all stratified by parental income percentile, race, and gender. Data files are downloadable in Stata and Excel formats from the Opportunity Insights website, with a full replication package on Harvard Dataverse (DOI: 10.7910/DVN/NALG3E) and an interactive tool at opportunityatlas.org.

---

### 477. Mobility Report Cards — College-Level Economic Mobility Data

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, higher-ed, longitudinal, college-access
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/undermatching/

A comprehensive college-level dataset linking anonymized federal administrative records to measure income mobility at U.S. colleges, including students' earnings in their thirties, parents' income levels, ACT/SAT scores, and IPEDS/College Scorecard institution characteristics across multiple birth cohorts. The data enable analysis of which colleges function as engines of economic mobility and at what rates, enabling comparisons of mobility rates and access patterns by income quintile. Individual data tables (15 in total) are available in Stata and Excel formats, with a full replication package on Harvard Dataverse; an interactive New York Times visualization also accompanies the release.

---

### 478. College-Level Data for 139 Selective American Colleges

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, higher-ed, longitudinal, college-access
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/collegeadmissions/

A dataset covering 139 selective U.S. colleges, linking anonymized admissions records with income tax data and SAT/ACT scores to analyze the determinants of admission and the causal effects of attendance on socioeconomic outcomes. The data support analysis of how parental income influences admission rates at elite institutions and the downstream earnings consequences of attending selective versus non-selective colleges. Freely available in CSV and Stata formats with an accompanying codebook; an interactive New York Times visualization ("How Income Influences College Attendance") accompanies the release.

---

### 479. Social Capital Atlas — County, ZIP, High School, and College Data

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, college-access
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/social-capital-i-measurement-and-associations-with-economic-mobility/

A dataset measuring three dimensions of social capital — economic connectedness between high- and low-SES individuals, social cohesion (clique formation in friendship networks), and civic engagement (volunteering rates) — derived from analysis of 21 billion Facebook friendships. Data are available at the county, ZIP code, high school, and college levels, including a 100×100 friending-rate matrix across socioeconomic groups, enabling research on which communities provide cross-class social ties that support upward income mobility. All files are freely downloadable in CSV format from opportunityinsights.org/data/ with an interactive Social Capital Atlas at socialcapital.org.

---

### 480. Who Becomes an Inventor — Innovation Rates by Childhood Location and Demographics

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, longitudinal
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/losteinsteins/

A dataset tracking more than one million U.S. inventors by linking patent records to tax records and school district records, providing innovation rates organized by childhood commuting zone and state, gender, parental income quintile, educational institution attended, and career trajectory including income distributions. The data reveal that children from high-income families are significantly more likely to become inventors, largely due to exposure to innovation rather than innate ability — the so-called "lost Einsteins" phenomenon. Available in Stata, Excel, and README formats as individual tables and a bundled ZIP, with a full replication package on Harvard Dataverse.

---

### 481. Race and Economic Opportunity — Intergenerational Mobility by Race

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, longitudinal, college-access
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/race/

A dataset derived from de-identified longitudinal records covering nearly the entire U.S. population from 1989 to 2015, measuring intergenerational income mobility and related outcomes disaggregated by race, gender, and parental income percentile at the national, commuting zone, and county levels. Data tables include national statistics by parent income percentile and race, income transition matrices, and estimates for second-generation immigrants by country of origin, as well as intergenerational educational attainment matrices. Files are downloadable in Stata and Excel formats; a full replication package is available on GitHub and Harvard Dataverse.

---

### 482. Changing Opportunity — County and Commuting Zone Trend Data (1978–1992 Cohorts)

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, longitudinal
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/changingopportunity/

A dataset covering birth cohorts from 1978 to 1992 at the county, commuting zone, and national levels, tracking trends in earnings, educational attainment, standardized test scores, and mortality rates by parental income, race, and gender over time. The data document growing class gaps and shrinking race gaps in economic opportunity across these cohorts and include a crosswalk converting income percentiles to 2023 dollars. All tables are freely downloadable in CSV and Stata formats with PDF codebooks from the Opportunity Insights website.

---

### 483. Geography of Intergenerational Mobility — Commuting Zone and County Data

Type: dataset | Source: Harvard University
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, longitudinal, college-access
URL: https://opportunityinsights.org/paper/land-of-opportunity/

A foundational dataset analyzing intergenerational income mobility using administrative records from more than 40 million children and their parents, covering commuting zones, counties, and metropolitan statistical areas across the United States. In addition to mobility statistics and income transition matrices, the dataset includes community characteristics correlated with upward mobility — school quality, segregation levels, income inequality, social capital, and family stability — supporting causal analysis of place effects on children's outcomes. Data are available in Excel and Stata formats (10 online tables) with a bundled replication package; full dataset on Harvard Dataverse (DOI: 10.7910/DVN/NALG3E).

---

### 484. NSC High School Benchmarks — Postsecondary Outcomes Data Appendix

Type: dataset | Source: National Student Clearinghouse
Tags: open-datasets, higher-ed, k-12, longitudinal, college-access, dropout-prevention
URL: https://nscresearchcenter.org/high-school-benchmarks/

An annually updated Excel data appendix accompanying the NSC High School Benchmarks report (13th edition in 2025), providing postsecondary enrollment, first-year persistence, and six-year credential completion rates for three high school graduating classes (2024, 2022, and 2018 respectively). Outcomes are disaggregated by high school characteristics including income level, minority enrollment percentage, and geographic locale, enabling comparisons between high- and low-poverty schools; for example, STEM completion rates ranged from 8.1% at high-poverty schools to 22.4% at low-poverty schools for the class of 2018. The 2025 data appendix is directly downloadable as an XLSX file from the report page, with prior-year appendices available back to at least 2022.

---

### 485. NSC Some College, No Credential — National and State Outcomes Data

Type: dataset | Source: National Student Clearinghouse
Tags: open-datasets, higher-ed, longitudinal, dropout-prevention, college-access
URL: https://nscresearchcenter.org/some-college-no-credential/

Downloadable Excel appendices from the NSC Some College, No Credential (SCNC) annual report series, providing national and state-level data on the tens of millions of U.S. adults who left higher education without a postsecondary credential. The National/State Data appendix covers demographic profiles and state SCNC populations and outcomes; the National Outcomes Data appendix tracks re-enrollment rates, credential completion, and persistence across states and institutional sectors. Annual data are available for 2022, 2023, 2024, and 2025 in XLSX format, supplemented by interactive Tableau dashboards; historical reports extend back to 2014.

---

### 486. Urban Institute Education Data Portal — API Documentation and Data Sources

Type: dataset | Source: Urban Institute
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, longitudinal
URL: https://educationdata.urban.org/documentation/

The full API documentation for the Urban Institute's Education Data Portal, which harmonizes and provides unified programmatic access to six major federal education datasets: the Common Core of Data (CCD) school directory and enrollment data, the Civil Rights Data Collection, the Small Area Income and Poverty Estimates, IPEDS postsecondary institution data, the College Scorecard, and the National Historical Geographic Information System (NHGIS). The API supports queries by education level (schools, districts, colleges), geography, time frame, and indicator; code interfaces are available for Stata, R, Python, and JavaScript. Data are openly accessible without authentication for most endpoints; the documentation page lists all currently available endpoints and variables.

---

### 487. Current Population Survey (CPS) Data at NBER

Type: dataset | Source: NBER
Tags: open-datasets, k-12, higher-ed, longitudinal
URL: https://www.nber.org/research/data/current-population-survey-cps-data-nber

The NBER's maintained archive of the U.S. Current Population Survey, the federal government's primary monthly survey of labor force participation and employment, spanning basic monthly data from 1976 to the present and CPS supplements from 1964 onward. The archive includes the Merged Outgoing Rotation Groups (MORG) files for earnings analysis, the Mare-Winship standardized subsets (1964–1992), and thematic supplement extracts covering schooling, fertility, immigration, and income — making it a key source for longitudinal analysis of educational attainment and its labor market returns. All files are freely downloadable from the NBER website with SAS, SPSS, and Stata data definition files and comprehensive methodology documentation.

### 506. Analyzing Strategies in MATHia with BERT

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: math-strategies, nlp, aims, carnegie-learning
URL: https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1007/978-3-031-98465-5_15

Presents ASTRA (AI-based Strategy Analysis), which uses BERT-based representation learning to discover and analyze math problem-solving strategies at scale in intelligent tutoring system data. The researchers pre-trained BERT using masked language modeling on 6th and 7th-grade student action sequences from Carnegie Learning's MATHia platform, then fine-tuned the embeddings to distinguish successful from unsuccessful strategies. Results showed that single-task strategies predominantly led to success while mixed-task approaches were associated with unsuccessful attempts, with the fine-tuned model achieving approximately 80% accuracy.

---

### 507. "Can A Language Model Represent Math Strategies?": Learning Math Strategies from Big Data using BERT

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: math-strategies, nlp, aims
URL: https://dl.acm.org/doi/10.1145/3706468.3706558

Demonstrates that BERT-based language models can learn mathematical learning strategies at scale using student interaction data. The model is pre-trained using masked language modeling to learn strategy embeddings, then fine-tuned to predict whether students will apply correct problem-solving approaches. Testing across 655 schools showed that strategies learned from one school sample could be effectively adapted with minimal examples to accurately forecast student behavior in other schools.

---

### 508. De-identifying Student Personally Identifying Information in Discussion Forum Posts with Large Language Models

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: pii-privacy, llm-application, aims
URL: https://www.emerald.com/ils/article/126/5-6/401/1246753/De-identifying-student-personally-identifying

Evaluates the effectiveness of three large language models (GPT-4o, Llama 3.3 70B, and Llama 3.1 8B) in redacting personally identifying information from discussion forum posts in massive open online courses. All models achieved high recall rates exceeding 0.9, successfully identifying PII instances overlooked by humans, but precision was considerably lower (0.262 to 0.579) due to over-redaction of non-PII names and locations. The findings suggest LLMs show promise for de-identification tasks, particularly through hybrid human-AI approaches, though context-dependent performance variations indicate careful evaluation is necessary for new applications.

---

### 509. De-Identifying Student Personally Identifying Information with GPT-4

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: pii-privacy, llm-application, genai, aims
URL: https://educationaldatamining.org/edm2024/proceedings/2024.EDM-short-papers.57/2024.EDM-short-papers.57.pdf

Evaluates GPT-4's performance in de-identifying student data from 9 Massive Open Online Courses, achieving an average recall of 0.958 for identifying personally identifying information requiring redaction. The tool successfully identifies cases missed by humans during the redaction process, indicating GPT-4 can increase efficiency and enhance quality. However, precision is considerably worse (0.526), with over-redaction of names and locations that do not represent PII, showing a need for further improvement.

---

### 510. Mathematics Teachers' Use of Generative AI to Create Active Learning Experiences

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: math-education, genai, aims
URL: https://socialinnovationsjournal.com/index.php/sij/article/view/9994

Examines 16 mathematics teachers using generative AI to modify classroom tasks for generative (active) learning and to engage in novel lesson design activities. Teachers valued the creative potential of generative AI for developing such activities but expressed concerns regarding efficiency, usability, accuracy, and broader systemic considerations. The authors present five policy and practice recommendations based on their findings.

### 511. Parsing Coaching Practice: A Systematic Framework for Describing Coaching Discourse

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: coaching, aims
URL: https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/epub/10.1177/23328584241263861

Addresses a significant gap in the coaching literature by developing a taxonomy of coaching "moves" that breaks down specific discourse strategies used by professional learning coaches. The research identifies two key problems: limited comparative evidence about coaching effectiveness, and the field's tendency to focus on abstract concepts like trust-building rather than concrete communication techniques. The proposed taxonomy offers practitioners a shared vocabulary for understanding coach discourse patterns, potentially supporting future investigations into how coaching interactions influence teacher development.

---

### 512. Teaching Teachers to Use Computer Assisted Learning Effectively: Experimental and Quasi-Experimental Evidence

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: computer-assisted-learning, k-12, rct, aims
URL: https://www.nber.org/papers/w32388

Examines a program providing weekly coaching to help educators implement computer-assisted learning for customized student progress in elementary and middle school mathematics. Two field experiments showed significant gains of 0.12-0.22 standard deviations in math performance. The research reveals that meaningful improvements occurred when students received at least 35 minutes of weekly practice, with success factors including strong teacher buy-in, clear implementation timing, and consistent monitoring of student progress with targeted intervention for struggling learners.

---

### 513. The Promises and Pitfalls of Using Language Models to Measure Instruction Quality in Education

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: nlp, llm-application, aims
URL: https://aclanthology.org/2024.naacl-long.246/

Examines how NLP techniques can assess instructional practices across K-12 classrooms and pre-service teacher settings. Pretrained language models performed comparably to human raters when evaluating simpler, discrete teaching behaviors but struggled with more complex practices requiring higher-level inference. Notably, analyzing only teacher speech yielded strong results for measuring student-centered approaches, reducing concerns about obtaining quality student speech transcriptions.

---

### 514. Using a Multi-Agent System and Evidence-Centered Design to Integrate Educator Expertise Within Generated Feedback

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: automated-feedback, genai, aims
URL: https://www.mdpi.com/2227-7102/15/10/1273

Proposes a framework for using generative AI to facilitate mathematics teacher learning through automated rehearsals where educators practice teaching skills, obtain feedback, and enhance their methods. The approach has three components: leveraging evidence-centered design modeling to create templates capturing mathematics teaching complexity, converting expertise from these templates into GenAI prompts, and employing a multi-agent system that distributes this expertise across agents to maintain sophistication while simulating rehearsals and delivering feedback.

### 516. New Study Finds Every Minute Spent on Khan Academy Can Lead to Learning Gains

Type: blog-post | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: khan-academy, k-12, aims
URL: https://blog.khanacademy.org/new-study-finds-every-minute-spent-on-khan-academy-can-lead-to-learning-gains/

Khan Academy researchers conducted a within-subjects study tracking 100,000 students across two school years and found that increased platform usage correlated with improved MAP Growth test scores. The study design compared each student to themselves over time, eliminating confounding factors like motivation. The findings demonstrate that even modest increases in Khan Academy usage translate to measurable learning gains across different grades and demographics.

### 517. Three Research-Backed Strategies Teachers Can Implement on Khan Academy to Boost Student Learning Outcomes

Type: blog-post | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: khan-academy, k-12, aims
URL: https://blog.khanacademy.org/three-research-backed-strategies-teachers-can-implement-on-khan-academy-to-boost-student-learning-outcomes/

Identifies three effective teaching strategies from Khan Academy research: prioritizing Course Mastery Goals to ensure skill development with minimal teacher effort, using supplemental assignments sparingly to address specific gaps rather than duplicating content, and maintaining a regular usage pattern for consistent student success both on the platform and on external assessments.

### 518. University of Toronto Randomized Controlled Trial of 11K Students Demonstrates a Meaningful Positive Effect of Khan Academy on Student Learning

Type: blog-post | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: khan-academy, rct, aims
URL: https://blog.khanacademy.org/university-of-toronto-randomized-controlled-trial-of-11k-students-demonstrates-a-meaningful-positive-effect-of-khan-academy-on-student-learning/

A University of Toronto randomized controlled trial involving 11,000 students found that elementary students (grades 3-6) who used Khan Academy for approximately 35 minutes weekly showed 0.12 to 0.17 standard deviations higher math assessment scores. The study demonstrated meaningful learning improvements when teachers prioritized consistent platform usage, though middle school students saw fewer gains due to lower engagement levels.

### 519. Why Khan Academy Will Be Using "Skills to Proficient" to Measure Learning Outcomes

Type: blog-post | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: khan-academy, formative-assessment, aims
URL: https://blog.khanacademy.org/why-khan-academy-will-be-using-skills-to-proficient-to-measure-learning-outcomes/

Khan Academy is adopting "skills to proficient" as its primary metric for measuring student learning, as research shows this indicator correlates with standardized math assessments better than time spent alone. The approach aligns with mastery learning principles, emphasizing that students achieve deeper understanding by reaching higher proficiency levels on fewer skills rather than attempting many skills at shallow levels.

### 523. Finding Belonging: The Search for Comprehensive Measurements of Student Belonging in Math

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: student-belonging, math-education, lsu, aims
URL: https://repository.lsu.edu/srec_reports/18/

Presents Phase One findings on developing an instrument to measure belonging in mathematics. Encompasses a review and assessment of existing belonging instruments, along with insights from a panel discussion regarding how school-aged students perceive belonging. Key deliverables include a comprehensive definition of belonging, an inventory of current instruments, a multidimensional framework accounting for context and perspective, validated items from existing scales, and a definitionally grounded recommended set of belonging items for future piloting, testing, and validation.

### 525. Analyzing Math Learning Strategies at Scale using AI Representations

Type: presentation | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: math-strategies, nlp, aims
URL: https://aera25-aera.ipostersessions.com/default.aspx?s=19-AD-E5-B0-78-EB-BC-70-51-B2-77-D5-9E-76-70-D0&guestview=true

AERA 2025 poster presenting ASTRA (AI-based Strategy Analysis), which uses representation learning methods to discover patterns in ITS data for analyzing math strategies. Adapted BERT models to learn representations of math strategies from large-scale 6th and 7th-grade data collected from Carnegie Learning's MATHia platform. By observing sequences of student actions, BERT was pre-trained in an unsupervised manner to understand hidden structure within action sequences, then fine-tuned embeddings enabled identification of correct strategies and analysis of strategy effectiveness.

### 528. Linguistic Features Predicting Math Word Problem Readability Among Less-Skilled Readers

Type: paper | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: math-word-problems, nlp, aims
URL: https://educationaldatamining.org/EDM2025/proceedings/2025.EDM.short-papers.189/index.html

Investigates which linguistic features predict math word problem readability for struggling readers, using data from 297,072 students in an intelligent tutoring system. A random forest model achieved the best performance (AUC = .75), revealing that traditional readability metrics were not important to the model's performance. Instead, word count emerged as the most predictive feature, followed by custom semantic magnitude and lexical diversity measures, suggesting that specialized readability assessments for math problems differ substantially from conventional approaches.

This June 2025 presentation by researchers at Louisiana State University updated psychometric analyses of the Math Mind Measures (MMM) scale, a tool for assessing mathematical thinking. ### 535. Best Practices: Running Focus Groups with Young Children

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, qualitative-research, early-childhood, lsu
URL: https://repository.lsu.edu/srec_reports/26/

This practice guide by H. Colleen Sinclair offers recommendations for conducting focus groups with elementary school students. The resource was developed to help researchers gather students' experiences with mathematics instruction, particularly regarding their engagement with digital learning tools in classrooms. It presents practical, accessible guidance for qualitative research with young participants.

---

### 536. Educator Perceptions of Working with DreamBox Learning

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, digital-learning-platforms, lsu
URL: https://repository.lsu.edu/srec_reports/21/

This research report evaluates how K-12 educators experienced implementing DreamBox Learning, a digital math platform, in their classrooms. The study gathered feedback through focus groups to understand what worked well and what challenges emerged, with particular attention to how the technology affected both student engagement and teaching practices.

---

### 537. English Learner Reclassification Policy Structures and Student Characteristics

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, english-learners, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2024/06/25/english-learner-reclassification-policy-structures-and-student-characteristics/

This research brief examines how English Learner reclassification policies vary across states and their relationship to student demographics. The authors analyze four distinct groups of state policies based on the kind of reclassification requirements and find that states with larger EL populations tend to implement more complex policies, while those experiencing faster EL growth rely more on English language proficiency assessments alone.

---

### 538. English Learner Reclassification Policy Structures and Student Outcomes

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, english-learners, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2024/11/05/english-learner-reclassification-policy-structures-and-student-outcomes/

This research brief examines how policy complexity in English Learner reclassification varies across four states and affects student outcomes. The study finds that students in states with more complex reclassification policies are less likely to be eligible for reclassification, particularly when non-English language proficiency assessments are included as requirements. The analysis suggests that more stringent policies may create barriers prolonging EL student status.

---

### 539. Exploring the Impact of School Discipline and Attendance on Academic Achievement

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, school-discipline, attendance, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2025/05/05/exploring-the-impact-of-school-discipline-and-attendance-on-academic-achievement/

This research brief examines how disciplinary actions and attendance patterns affect academic growth among over 66,000 elementary students in a large U.S. school district. The study found that attendance rate was a strong and consistent predictor of academic growth in both math and reading, while suspensions negatively impacted math achievement, underscoring the importance of equitable discipline practices and attendance support.

---

### 540. Geaux Math! EBRPSS & LSU: Differentiating Lessons with AI

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, math-education, genai, lsu
URL: https://repository.lsu.edu/srec_reports/12/

This report examines a pilot program created by East Baton Rouge Parish School System and Louisiana State University to explore how generative AI tools can help teachers develop differentiated math instruction for K-8 students. The study, funded by the Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation, analyzed the impact on teachers' levels of self-efficacy with new technology and their capacity to address diverse student needs while managing burnout.

---

### 541. How Digital Platforms Provide Individualized Learning Experiences in Mathematics

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, digital-learning-platforms, math-education, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2024/06/27/how-digital-platforms-provide-individualized-learning-experiences-in-mathematics/

This research report examines how a digital learning platform delivers personalized math instruction to approximately 2.7 million students in grades 1-5. The study analyzes assessment feedback mechanisms that adapt learning pathways based on student placement levels, demonstrating that students' experiences with digital learning platforms are individualized and responsive to their math learning needs.

---

### 542. Investing Early: The Impact of State Prekindergarten Funding on Kindergarten Academic Outcomes

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, prekindergarten, early-childhood, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2025/06/30/investing-early-the-impact-of-state-prekindergarten-funding-on-kindergarten-academic-outcomes/

This research examines how state-level investment in pre-K programs for four-year-olds correlates with kindergarten math achievement across 31 school districts in nine states. Using data from over 200,000 students, the study found that kindergarten math growth was strongest in states with consistently high levels of PreK4 investment, and that overall district performance history proved to be a stronger predictor of success than pre-K enrollment alone.

---

### 543. Math Performance in East Baton Rouge Parish Schools: 2023-2024

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, math-education, lsu
URL: https://repository.lsu.edu/srec_reports/23/

This research report examines how a digital learning platform and student motivation factors influence math achievement among middle school students in Louisiana. The study analyzes key motivational factors such as confidence and anxiety, digital learning use, and student characteristics to identify intervention strategies that could strengthen student confidence and reduce math anxiety.

---

### 544. Measuring Motivation, Improving Engagement

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, math-motivation, lsu
URL: https://repository.lsu.edu/srec_reports/19/

This report addresses the challenge of assessing student motivation in mathematics by integrating existing measurement tools and piloting them across two diverse student populations. The authors developed 10 reliable scales to evaluate different aspects of math motivation, with the goal of constructing reliable scales of pertinent individual differences in math motivation to facilitate discussion about validity and classroom applications.

---

### 545. New Normal in Early Elementary Mathematics Learning: Part III -- Learning from Variation in Grade 3

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, math-education, k-12, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2024/12/19/new-normal-in-early-elementary-mathematics-learning-part-iii-learning-from-variation-in-grade-3/

This research examines mathematics learning growth trajectories for third-graders using data from over 6,000 schools. The study found that disparities in student growth persist across school years, with Grade 3 emerging as a potential turning point where initial achievement gaps may begin to widen between students who started at different levels.

---

### 546. New Normal in Early Elementary Mathematics Learning: Part II -- School-level Variation in Growth in Grades 1 and 2

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, math-education, k-12, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2024/06/25/new-normal-in-early-elementary-mathematics-learning-part-ii-school-level-variation-in-growth-in-grades-1-and-2/

This research examines variations in mathematics learning growth across schools for students in first and second grade during the 2021-2022 and 2022-2023 school years. Using data from over 6,000 schools and the i-Ready Diagnostic assessment tool, the study explores how school demographic characteristics relate to student achievement patterns and identifies that learning growth fluctuates year-to-year.

---

### 547. New Normal in Early Elementary Mathematics Learning: Part I -- Initial Findings on Growth and Domains in Grade 1 through Grade 2

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, math-education, k-12, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2024/06/25/new-normal-in-early-elementary-mathematics-learning-part-i-initial-findings-on-growth-and-domains-in-grade-1-through-grade-2/

This research study examines mathematics learning outcomes for over 6,000 schools using adaptive assessment data from students who entered first grade in fall 2021. The analysis reveals that learning growth is greatest in the first half of students' first-grade year and identifies significant disparities in student progression, while highlighting Algebra and Algebraic Thinking as the strongest predictor of overall mathematical growth in early elementary grades.

---

### 548. The Math Mind Measures: A User Guide

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, math-motivation, lsu
URL: https://repository.lsu.edu/srec_reports/16/

This user guide presents a comprehensive survey instrument designed to assess math motivation in students. The guide documents the development of the Math Mind Measures (MMM) across multiple forms, including long-forms with 138 items, short-forms with 77 items, brief versions, and parallel forms, created through piloting with diverse student populations across different grade levels and school districts.

---

### 549. Toward a Common Research Framework for Professional Learning

Type: framework | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, professional-development, rppl
URL: https://rpplpartnership.org/external-resource/toward-a-common-research-framework-for-pl/

This report documents findings from interviews with professional learning organizations within the RPPL network, focusing on how these groups manage and utilize data. The framework aims to advance four key objectives: creating standardized measurement tools across professional learning organizations, broadening access to shared data, establishing secure infrastructure for data storage, and developing innovative, cost-effective research measures.

### 550. Understanding the Impact of Educators' Social-Emotional Learning (SEL) Skills on Student Academic Growth

Type: report | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, sel, professional-development, northwestern-e4
URL: https://e4.northwestern.edu/2024/08/21/understanding-the-impact-of-educators-social-emotional-learning-sel-skills-on-student-academic-growth/

This research brief investigates how teachers' social-emotional competencies, specifically emotion regulation and relationship management, correlate with student academic outcomes. The study analyzed survey data from 269 K-8 educators and found associations between teacher demographics and their SEL skills, while also examining how educator well-being relates to their emotional capabilities and perceptions of school climate.

### 551. Curriculum & Learning Improvement Project (CLIP)

Type: project-website | Source: AIMS Collaboratory
Tags: aims, data-sharing, norc
URL: https://www.norc.org/research/projects/curriculum-and-learning-improvement-project-clip.html

CLIP is an innovative data ecosystem developed by NORC at the University of Chicago for the Gates Foundation that integrates learning management systems and curriculum data to provide educators with real-time insights on middle school math instruction. The project enables teachers, principals, and school district leaders to link curriculum implementation to student outcomes and make more informed instructional decisions, while also supporting researchers in conducting evaluations more efficiently.

---

### 552. ALTER-Math: AI-augmented Learning by Teaching to Enhance and Renovate Math Learning

Type: platform | Source: LEVI Math
Tags: learning-engineering, math-education, genai, k-12
URL: https://learning-engineering-virtual-institute.org/teams/alter-math/

ALTER-Math is a platform that helps middle school students strengthen their math understanding by teaching an AI "student." As learners explain concepts, correct mistakes, and guide their virtual peer, they engage in a research-based educational approach that combines personalization, motivational strategies, and evidence-based feedback to make math learning more accessible and effective for all students.

### 553. Khanmigo by Khan Academy

Type: platform | Source: LEVI Math
Tags: learning-engineering, math-education, genai-tutoring, khan-academy, k-12
URL: https://learning-engineering-virtual-institute.org/teams/khan-academy/

The Khan Academy LEVI team develops Khanmigo, an AI-powered tutoring system designed to help students practice math skills with personalized support and feedback. The platform addresses a critical gap in classrooms where students often lack sufficient practice opportunities and immediate guidance when they struggle. By combining AI tutoring with teacher insights and data, the team aims to significantly improve student math performance across early grades and middle school levels.

---

### 554. PLUS Tutoring by Carnegie Mellon University

Type: platform | Source: LEVI Math
Tags: learning-engineering, math-education, intelligent-tutoring, k-12
URL: https://learning-engineering-virtual-institute.org/teams/carnegie-mellon-university/

PLUS (Personalized Learning Squared) Tutoring combines human tutors, student math software, and AI analytics to deliver targeted tutoring support during the school day. The platform analyzes student practice data to identify struggling students and allocate tutors strategically, reducing costs while maintaining one-on-one interaction. By focusing scarce human tutoring where it has the biggest impact, the system aims to scale high-quality instruction and improve equity in learning outcomes.

---

### 555. Eedi: Misconceptions Map

Type: platform | Source: LEVI Math
Tags: learning-engineering, math-education, personalized-learning, k-12
URL: https://learning-engineering-virtual-institute.org/teams/eedi/

Eedi develops an AI-powered "Misconceptions Map" that analyzes student math errors to identify root conceptual gaps and predict future learning struggles. The system uses a knowledge graph to track how math concepts interconnect, recommending personalized learning steps for each student. A randomized controlled trial involving 3,000 students across 20 schools demonstrated that using Eedi led to 2-4 months of additional learning gain in an academic year.

---

### 556. MATHstream by Carnegie Learning

Type: platform | Source: LEVI Math
Tags: learning-engineering, math-education, genai, carnegie-learning, k-12
URL: https://learning-engineering-virtual-institute.org/teams/carnegie-learning/

MATHstream is an interactive, adaptive live-video platform that pairs middle school students with expert instructors for real-time math problem-solving. The system incorporates generative AI supports for audio, video, and text chat to help students recover missed learning and build math proficiency, while also assisting teachers with lesson preparation and professional development. Districts in Massachusetts and Texas demonstrated significant gains, with students completing just 3-5 sessions achieving notable score improvements on state assessments.

---

### 557. HAT: Hybrid Human-Agent Tutoring

Type: platform | Source: LEVI Math
Tags: learning-engineering, math-education, intelligent-tutoring, k-12
URL: https://learning-engineering-virtual-institute.org/teams/university-of-colorado-boulder/

HAT is an AI-powered platform developed by the University of Colorado Boulder and Saga Education that analyzes small-group tutoring sessions to provide tutors with data-driven feedback on their discourse practices. The system helps scale high-impact human tutoring while maintaining quality by giving tutors specific and directed feedback to improve their instructional techniques and ultimately enhance student math achievement in Title 1 schools.

---

### 558. Rori by Rising Academies

Type: platform | Source: LEVI Math
Tags: learning-engineering, math-education, genai-tutoring, k-12
URL: https://learning-engineering-virtual-institute.org/teams/rising-academy-network/

Rori is an AI-powered WhatsApp chatbot that delivers personalized math tutoring via conversational interactions. The platform uses natural language processing and machine learning to assess student ability and deliver scaffolded lessons across Grades 1-9, enabling learning gains for under $5 per student annually without requiring high-speed internet or advanced devices. Field testing in Ghana showed the platform more than doubled learning gains among approximately 500 students over six months.

---

### 559. TLA Educational AI Leaderboard

Type: platform | Source: The Learning Agency
Tags: learning-engineering, tla
URL: https://the-learning-agency.com/guides-resources/leaderboard-datasets-report/

Educational AI evaluation platform featuring benchmarks designed around real educational tasks with private test sets to prevent data contamination. Includes ASAP 2.0 (automated scoring of student persuasive essays) and the Eedi Misconception Annotation Project (identifying student math misconceptions), with performance, cost, and latency comparisons across models.

---

### 560. FAB-AI Pedagogy Benchmark Leaderboard

Type: platform | Source: AI-for-Education.org
Tags: learning-engineering, higher-ed
URL: https://www.fab-ai.org/initiatives/ai-for-education/edtech-quality/benchmarks

Pedagogy benchmark leaderboard evaluating 220+ AI models from OpenAI, Anthropic, Google, Meta, and others on education tasks for low- and middle-income countries. Includes downloadable CSV results, a quality assurance facility, and task-specific AI evaluation capabilities. Maintained by FAB-AI through their AI-for-Education.org initiative.

---

### 561. TutorBench

Type: platform | Source: Scale AI
Tags: intelligent-tutoring, genai
URL: https://labs.scale.com/leaderboard/tutorbench

Benchmark evaluating LLM tutoring capabilities across adaptive explanation generation, assessment and feedback, and active learning support in STEM subjects. Features 1,490 expert-curated prompts (56% multimodal) with 15,220 rubric criteria scored by an automated LLM judge achieving 78% agreement with human raters. The best-performing model scores only 55.7%, indicating tutoring remains a challenging frontier for AI.

---

### 562. MathTutorBench

Type: platform | Source: ETH Zurich
Tags: math-education, intelligent-tutoring, genai
URL: https://eth-lre.github.io/mathtutorbench/

Benchmark assessing open-ended pedagogical capabilities of LLM tutors in mathematics through seven tasks organized around three teacher competencies: problem solving, Socratic questioning, and solution correctness evaluation. Published as an EMNLP 2025 Oral paper. Key finding: subject-matter expertise does not translate to effective teaching. Code, data, and a pedagogical reward model are openly available under CC BY 4.0.

---

### 563. pyBKT — Python Bayesian Knowledge Tracing

Type: code | Source: UC Berkeley CAHLR
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring
URL: https://github.com/CAHLR/pyBKT

Python library implementing Bayesian Knowledge Tracing and variants for modeling student cognitive mastery from problem-solving sequences. Supports individual student priors, item-specific parameters, and resource-based learning rates with a scikit-learn-style API. Includes optimized C++ backend reducing fitting time from 1.5 hours to 45 seconds for 5,000 students. Published at EDM 2021, 254 stars, MIT license.

---

### 564. pyKT — Deep Learning Knowledge Tracing Toolkit

Type: code | Source: pyKT Team
Tags: learning-engineering, intelligent-tutoring
URL: https://github.com/pykt-team/pykt-toolkit

PyTorch-based library providing standardized preprocessing, training, and evaluation for 29+ deep learning knowledge tracing models including DKT, DKVMN, SAKT, SAINT, and AKT across 7+ datasets. Published at NeurIPS 2022 with hyperparameter tuning results. 397 stars, MIT license.

---

### 565. py-irt — Bayesian Item Response Theory

Type: code | Source: University of Notre Dame
Tags: learning-engineering, formative-assessment
URL: https://github.com/nd-ball/py-irt

Python library implementing Bayesian IRT models using variational inference, supporting 1PL (Rasch), 2PL, and 4PL models with vague or hierarchical priors. Provides CLI and programmatic interfaces for training and evaluation on scored prediction datasets. Published in INFORMS Journal on Computing 2023, 167 stars, MIT license.

---

### 566. ADL xAPI Wrapper

Type: code | Source: ADL Initiative
Tags: learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms
URL: https://github.com/adlnet/xAPIWrapper

Official JavaScript client library from the Advanced Distributed Learning Initiative (U.S. Department of Defense) for communicating with xAPI-compliant Learning Record Stores. Handles statement creation, activity states, agent profiles, attachments, and authentication. 223 stars, Apache 2.0 license.

---

### 567. ADL Learning Record Store

Type: code | Source: ADL Initiative
Tags: learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms, data-sharing
URL: https://github.com/adlnet/ADL_LRS

Open-source reference implementation of a Learning Record Store for storing xAPI learning data, updated to align with IEEE 9274.1.1 (xAPI 2.0). Built in Python with Docker support, OAuth integration, and Nginx/uWSGI deployment options. 331 stars, Apache 2.0 license.

---

### 568. OATutor — Open-Source Adaptive Tutoring System

Type: code | Source: UC Berkeley CAHLR
Tags: intelligent-tutoring, personalized-learning, k-12
URL: https://github.com/CAHLR/OATutor

Open-source adaptive tutoring system using Bayesian Knowledge Tracing for skill mastery estimation, with scaffolded hints and intelligent problem selection. Built in React with optional Firebase logging, deployable to static hosting without a backend. Published at CHI 2023 with learning gains documented in PLOS ONE. 199 stars, MIT license (CC BY 4.0 for content).

---

### 569. Learning Commons — AI Developer Tools for Education

Type: platform | Source: Learning Commons
Tags: learning-engineering, digital-learning-platforms, genai
URL: https://docs.learningcommons.org/

Open developer platform providing research-backed resources for building instructionally grounded AI products. Offers a Knowledge Graph API combining curriculum data, academic standards, and learning science research, plus Evaluators for assessing AI-generated educational content quality (literacy, vocabulary, grade-level appropriateness). Includes MCP server integration, playground environments, and alignment with Illustrative Math curriculum.
